The Axe of Kolt

A Note For The Player:

This adventure game is very much "old school" in that the gameplay involves having to SEARCH objects and/or LOOK BEHIND, IN or UNDER objects to find objects that you will need during the game. You might also have to EXAMINE WALL to find something on it.

If you do not like this style of adventure gameplay then regrettably this game may not be for you.

Many thanks

Larry Horsfield

Please type the letter O then press Enter to Continue to the Start Options Page.

> o
THE AXE OF KOLT  Start-Up Options:

Press B (enter) to Begin the Adventure from the First Location.

Press P (enter) to read the Prologue and Playing Instructions.
(Recommended if starting this adventure for the first time)

If you have already started the adventure and wish to restart from a saved position, click on the Blue Folder Icon in the taskbar above.

PLEASE NOTE: This game was envisioned by the author as being playable Cyan On Black. Since ADRIFT does not support an authorial override of a player's colour preferences, be advised that if your background colour is not black, portions of this game will not be easily readable. For maximum experience as intended by the author please ensure your background colour is set to BLACK and the font colour to CYAN.

If you are visually impaired you can increase or decrease the font size whilst playing this game by holding down the CTRL key and moving your mouse wheel.

Before starting, please ensure that Autocomplete is unticked in the "Edit" tab in the taskbar above.

Useful Commands After The Adventure Has Started:

ABOUT : BUGS : COMMANDS : CREDITS : HELP
MACROS : MAP : SPEECH : VOCAB

> b

Crossroads
You are at a crossroad on the main highway that runs from north to south through the kingdom of Scippar. Here two other narrower roads head off to the East and West. By the side of the road is a freshly-painted signpost. The ground under your feet is covered in a layer of brown leaves which have fallen from the trees that surround you. Through the thickly clustered bare branches of the trees you can just about see, to the north, the mighty Droomdark mountains that form a spine across the continent.

You hear the haywain move off behind you, and turn to wave to the farmer, who gives you a nod and a thumbs-up for luck as he flicks his reins onto the backs of his oxen in a bid to encourage them to move a bit quicker.

> Read signpost
The four directional arms on the signpost read: North to Woolwych 6 km, South to Greenwych 4 km, East to Hengemire 1 km and West to Roffey 7 km.

> e
You move east.

Road to Hengemire
The road has now emerged from the woodland into open farmland. The farms and fields are marked by a network of drystone walls either side of the road. In the distance to the north, you see fields stretching away towards the foothills of the snow-peaked Droomdark mountains. The road continues East towards the village of Hengemire or you can go back West to the crossroads where you left the haywain.

> e
You move east.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs along the southern edge of Hengemire village green. On the South side of the road is the village cesspool with the church some distance further east. A wide, rutted track leads North from here along the west side of the green towards a large, sprawling building which you recognise as an inn and you can also go NE and SE, or East and West along the road. In the centre of the village green to the northeast you see a stone cross.

> e
You move east.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs through Hengemire along the southern edge of the village green. Directly North, in the centre of the green, you see a stone cross. The road continues East and West, the village cesspool is SW, the church SE, and to the South are the village stocks and pillory.

> e
You move east.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs along the south side of the village green. The road continues East out of the village, entering a forest about half a kilometre away. By the side of the road, almost hidden by the grass, is a milestone. To the South stands the village church, while some distance due North you see a well. You can also go North and NW onto the village green or West back along the road.

> read milestone
The inscription on the milestone has been badly worn by the elements but you see that it says "Chaldon 3 km" with an arrow pointing east underneath it.

> s
You move south.

By Old Church
You are in the southeast corner of the village green, standing by the door to the church, which leads South. Nearby is a gap that leads East through an iron fence into the village graveyard. The road through the village is to the North, NW or NE.

A woman comes out the church, wrapped in a cloak to ward off the cold wind. As she passes, you nod a greeting and smile. She looks at you with a slightly curious look on her face, but she returns your greeting with a nod and then hurries off towards the cottages on the north side of the green.

She is followed shortly after by several other villagers, some of whom pass you by without noticing you, but one or two glance in your direction and nod politely.

Finally, the vicar leaves the church and, shutting the door behind him, walks towards you. He is a surprisingly young man, probably in his late twenties, and as he passes you he doffs his hat and smiles. "God be with you, my friend," he says cheerily. You nod your head and reply in kind, and he walks away across the green, whistling merrily.

> e
You move east.

North End of Graveyard
You are at the north end of the graveyard, by the gap in the fence that leads West out to the church entrance. A cobbled path leading South divides the graveyard into two unequal halves containing lots of headstones.

You see a magpie perched on the top of one of the headstones at the south end of the graveyard. You notice it is holding a small object in its beak. As it sees you the bird takes wing but as it does so it drops the object it is holding in the grass by one of the headstones.

> read epitaphs
The epitaph on one headstone nearby makes you chuckle. It reads:

Here lies the body of Ezra Pound

Lost at sea and never found.

> s
You move south.

South End of Graveyard
You are at the south end of the graveyard, by the iron fence that marks the boundary. There are fewer graves at this end and you notice that the headstones are more recent. You can only go North along the path from here.

> read epitaphs
Just by the path stands a memorial stone that is almost obscured by the tall grass that grows uncut around it. The inscription on the stone reads:

Erected In Memory of Thomas Gear

Who was drowned in the river Sutlej

By a few affectionate friends

> search grass
You rummage in the tall grass and find the object that the magpie dropped, which you pick up - it is the clapper from inside a bell.

> n
You move north.

North End of Graveyard
You are at the north end of the graveyard, by the gap in the fence that leads West out to the church entrance. A cobbled path leading South divides the graveyard into two unequal halves containing lots of headstones.

> w
You move west.

By Old Church
You are in the southeast corner of the village green, standing by the door to the church, which leads South. Nearby is a gap that leads East through an iron fence into the village graveyard. The road through the village is to the North, NW or NE.

> n
You move north.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs along the south side of the village green. The road continues East out of the village, entering a forest about half a kilometre away. By the side of the road, almost hidden by the grass, is a milestone. To the South stands the village church, while some distance due North you see a well. You can also go North and NW onto the village green or West back along the road.

You hear a horse neigh and turn to see a brewer's dray, towed by two huge shire horses, come rumbling along the road from the west. As it approaches the village green, the drayman turns the horses north towards the inn. The dray trundles past the inn door, turns into the yard of the inn and is lost to sight.

> n
You move north.

SE Corner of Village Green
You stand on the southeast corner of the village green. On the other side of the road, due south, lies the village church. The eastern side of the village green is hemmed in by impenetrable vegetation with forest beyond that, but you can go North, NW, West and SW from here.

A man comes towards you pushing a wheelbarrow which has some stakes in it. He nods a greeting to you and proceeds to unload the contents of the wheelbarrow, which includes a length of rope and a sledgehammer.

As you watch he hammers one of the stakes upright into the ground then measures off 5 strides from the first stake and drives another stake into the earth. He then turns 90 degrees, measures off another 5 strides and drives another stake into the ground. He repeats this a third time to make a square.

Throwing the sledgehammer into the wheelbarrow, he picks up the rope and ties it to one of the stakes and then goes around the square of stakes, looping it over the other three before tying the rope off on the stake where he started.

Finally he takes a notice and a hammer from the wheelbarrow and nails the notice to one of the stakes. Placing the hammer back into the wheelbarrow, he picks up the handles and wheels the wheelbarrow off towards the cottages to the north of the green and he disappears behind one of them.

SE Corner of Village Green
You stand on the southeast corner of the village green. On the other side of the road, due south, lies the village church. The eastern side of the village green is hemmed in by impenetrable vegetation with forest beyond that, but you can go North, NW, West and SW from here. An area here has been roped off around four stakes, one of which has a notice nailed to it.

> read notice
The notice is printed at the top with "Hengemire Village Market" and underneath is written "Reserved for Awstin's fruit and vegetable stall for Tuesday".

> nw
You move northwest.

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.

> nw
You move northwest.

By Inn Yard
You are to the north of the inn, by the entrance to the yard which is West. Further North, NE and NW the cottages of the village folk lay huddled together with narrow paths between them. You can also go East and SE onto the village green or South along the track to the Inn door. In the yard of the inn to the west you see a brewer's dray.

You see the drayman come walking quickly out of the inn yard, looking furtively behind as he goes. He sees you watching him and puts his finger to his lips and winks - you realise that he is probably up to no good! However, you think to yourself that it is none of your business and you watch as he enters the huddle of cottages to the north. He knocks at the door of a small neat cottage, looking around to see if anyone else is watching him. The door opens and you catch a glimpse of a woman's face as the drayman slips inside and the door is closed behind him.

> w
You move west.

Inn Yard
You are to the north of the inn, in a large cobbled yard. On the west side of the yard there are storage sheds and to the north the stables. The track by the village green is to the East. Here you see a brewer's dray.

You see a man, probably the innkeeper, open the doors of a storage shed and go inside. He fetches out what looks like a large thick cushion and drops it by the side of the dray. He looks around as if seeking someone.

"Jonnie K!" he yells, "where are ya, ye lazy git?!". He waits a moment or two then, realising he is not going to get any help, he climbs up onto the dray and manhandles a barrel of ale from the top of the pile and rolls it so that it falls off the dray onto the cushion with a dull thud. He then jumps down and rolls the barrel towards the storage shed.

"I'll bloody murder that lazy bugger Jonnie!" you hear him mutter as he rolls the barrel into the storage shed. "Always skiving off when there's work to be done!"

> say hello to innkeeper
You say hello to the innkeeper. "Hello there!" he calls out to you. "Any chance you can give me a hand with these barrels?"

> help innkeeper
You offer to help the innkeeper unload the dray.

He is very grateful for your help and he tells you his name is William Roffey, better known as Billy. He offers you a bed for the night and all the food and ale you want in return for your help. The two of you spend the next hour or so unloading the dray and then loading it with empty barrels and crates of empty bottles.

No sooner have you finished than the drayman comes strolling round the corner, looking rather pleased with himself. The innkeeper sees him and, his face red with anger, yells at him.

"Where the 'ell 'ave you bin?! If it weren't fer this helpful geezer 'ere, I'd've 'ad ter unload that dray by meself!"

The drayman puts on an air of innocence and smiles at the two of you. "Sorry Billy, me old mate," he glibly says, "Had to visit my sick old muvver, I'm sure you don't begrudge her a little time with her favourite son?"

The innkeeper shakes his fist in the drayman's face. "Oh yeah!? Sick muvver my arse! More like visiting that floozy of yours! Now git back on that dray and get dem poor 'orses back to the brewery!"

The drayman, not wanting to outstay his welcome, hops up onto the seat of the dray and, flicking the reins onto the backs of the shires, guides them out of the inn yard and away back to Greenwych.

You do a few other odd jobs for the innkeeper and his wife Arabella, by which time the inn has opened and customers start to arrive. True to his word, you eat a hearty meal, cooked by Bella, as she is known to one and all, herself.

Later on you are relaxing in the inn, enjoying a pint of the excellent ale from Greenwych, which is the only good thing about the town you were last in.

East End of Inn
You are in the main room of the Dragonslayer's Arms inn. It is a large, dark room with a low, beamed ceiling and a stone floor strewn with rushes. Tallow candles gutter on several tables and on various places around the inn. The room smells of wine and ale, but it seems to be well-kept. Against the north wall are a row of barrels on trestles, in front of which is a plank of wood, supported by two tables, which is known as the "bar". The room extends West and the door leads Out.  The inn is full of villagers and travellers drinking and generally enjoying themselves.  Arabella Roffey is here.

You listen to the conversation amongst the villagers and your ears prick up at the mention of outlaws. You move closer to the people talking and learn that there is a band of outlaws in the forest to the east of Hengemire that are preying on travellers going to Chaldon and beyond.

> w
You move west.

West End of Inn
You are at the west end of the main room of the inn. This end of the room is dominated by a stone pit in which burns a blazing fire, the smoke from which rises errantly towards a chimney set above it on four square pillars. The south wall is covered by a large tapestry. Opposite that a door leads North and the other end of the room is East.

> x tapestry
The tapestry is quite large and depicts an army of human men fighting a horde of lizard-like men. The main figure is a giant of a man wielding a huge double-headed axe which glows with a nimbus of light. The tapestry is very dirty from the years of hanging in the smoky room and is splattered with holes where sparks from the fire have burnt it. Indeed, it could do with a good clean! In one corner of the tapestry you can just make out some writing underneath the dirt and grime.

Maybe it would be a better use of your time at this stage to talk to Arabella and ask her questions in order to get some information? You can always come back later and have a look around the inn.

> read writing
The writing reads: "King Kolt and his army fighting the Xixon hordes at the Battle of Domreil in the year 3745".

You think to yourself that as the year is now 3901, that was 146 years ago, long before your time. You vaguely remember hearing something about this battle several years ago when fighting in other lands, but you have never heard of the Xixon before.

> e
You move east.

East End of Inn
You are in the main room of the Dragonslayer's Arms inn. It is a large, dark room with a low, beamed ceiling and a stone floor strewn with rushes. Tallow candles gutter on several tables and on various places around the inn. The room smells of wine and ale, but it seems to be well-kept. Against the north wall are a row of barrels on trestles, in front of which is a plank of wood, supported by two tables, which is known as the "bar". The room extends West and the door leads Out.  The inn is full of villagers and travellers drinking and generally enjoying themselves.  Arabella Roffey is here.

> talk to bella
In between her serving other customers, you chat amicably to Bella and tell her something of your exploits as a mercenary swordsman. She tells you that the village could do with a few swordsmen to get rid of the outlaws who have infested the forest in recent weeks.

You see a small group of villagers get up from their table and don their coats. Bella bids them good night and they leave to go to their homes. As they open the door, an icy blast of wind blows in from outside, causing shouts of "Shut that door!" from other patrons. The door is slammed shut and everyone resumes their conversations.

> ask about outlaws
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the outlaws in the forest.

"They arrived about a month ago and started ambushing people travelling through the Old Forest alone and in small parties," she tells you. "We sent word to the garrison at Woolwych and they said that they would send some troops out to deal with them, but that hasn't happened yet. We've been able to get to Chaldon if we travel in a large party with armed guards, but there is a pass high in the foothills of the mountains which some people have been using, although it is often snowbound at this time of year and you wouldn't want to get stranded there at night because of the Dwark."

> ask about pass
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the pass in the mountains.

"It's quite high up," she tells you. "You just take the path north from the village and keep going past Magor's tower towards the mountains. You'll need warm clothing, it's often snowbound at this time of year and you definitely don't want to be there at night," she warns you. "A creature called a Dwark lives there."

> ask about dwark
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the Dwark in the pass.

"It's some sort of giant lizard I think," she tells you. "The trapper has seen it a few times, he nearly got caught by it once."

> ask about trapper
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the Trapper.

"He's a strange one, spends days if not weeks away in the hills and mountains trapping animals for their furs," she tells you. "I heard that he will be at the market tomorrow."

> ask about tapestry
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the tapestry.

"It's been up there for a very long time," she tells you. "Shows Kolt and his army defeating the Xixon at the battle of Domreil."

The innkeeper Billy Roffey comes out from the back of the inn with his daughter Sarah Ann and starts to play a soulful tune on a fiddle. Bella starts to sing a beautiful song about a maid and her lover, with Billy and Sarah Ann joining in the refrain. They have wonderful singing voices and you find yourself almost overwhelmed by the beauty of the music.

The song ends to a standing ovation from everyone and you yell for more along with many others. Billy and Sarah Ann make their bows and then return to whatever they were doing and only Bella is left in the main room.

> ask about magor
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about Magor.

"He is a sorcerer who lives in a tower up in the foothills north of here," she tells you. "People go to him for healing potions and the like. He comes down for a pint now and again, but he's getting on a bit now and we haven't seen him for a while."

> ask about old forest
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the forest.

"It's known as the Old Forest, as it has been there for thousands of years," she tells you. "It extends from the foothills of the mountains south to the river Sutlej. On the other side of the forest, to the east, is the village of Chaldon."

> ask about chaldon
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about Chaldon.

"Chaldon is the next village to the east," she tells you. "It's on the north bank of the Sutlej river. There's a ferry there which will take you across to the north of Hecate."

> ask about ferry
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the ferry at Chaldon.

"There's bloke there called Denny Joyce," she tells you. "He's got a boat and will ferry you across to Hecate for a fee."

> ask about ferryman
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the ferryman Denny Joyce.

"We were childhood sweethearts," she tells you, blushing ever so slightly. "I grew up in Chaldon but my family moved here when I was 19 and Denny and I grew apart. He married a local girl and I met Billy. Sadly his wife died in childbirth and they lost the baby as well. After that he turned to drink but manages to earn a living sailing people up and down the river and across to Hecate."

One of the villagers produces a squeeze box and starts to play a jaunty tune. Someone starts to sing along and others join in. Soon everyone, including yourself, is singing and clapping along with the tune. The song ends in a rousing chorus and everyone cheers. Bella refills everyone's tankards and glasses and there is a tot of rum for the squeeze box player.

You think to yourself that these are good folks and that settling in this village would not be such a bad idea.

> ask about kolt
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about Kolt.

"He was King Kelson's great-grandfather," she tells you. "Ruled Hecate a couple of hundred years ago."

> ask about xixon
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about the Xixon.

"I don't know much about them, way before my time," she tells you. "All I know is that they were lizards in human form."

> ask about kelson
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about King Kelson.

"He's only a young chap," she tells you. "He was crowned King of Hecate only last year after his father died."

> ask about father
(Arabella Roffey)

You ask Bella about King Kelson's father.

"He died last year," she tells you sadly. "He was a great king, loved by one and all."

There is a blast of cold air as the door opens, and a wet and bedraggled traveller enters the inn. Slamming the door behind him, he walks to the bar, buys a stiff drink and then sits down with some of the locals. He starts talking and from their shocked reaction, you gather it is grave news! As the crowd in the inn gather around the traveller, you also move closer so you can hear what is being said.

"...well anyway," the man tells everyone, taking a gulp of the whisky to steady his nerves. "I got away from Domreil just in time - the Xixon have returned to get their revenge on King Kelson!" There are gasps of horror from the listeners. "Seems they've invaded Hecate and laid siege to the city and King Kelson has issued a plea for anyone who might know where Kolt's tomb is to try and get word through. It seems the return of the Axe of Kolt is the only thing that's gonna save the city."

Billy the innkeeper looks worried. "If Kelson doan know where Kolt's tomb is, then nobody does," he tells the crowd of villagers. "I heard tell that the place where the tomb is was kept secret to prevent the axe falling into the wrong hands. Surely the Royal Family must know where it is?"

Dusty Miller chips in, "'Ang on! Some folks say it were Magor - y'know, the old sorcerer what lives up in the mountains - wot forged the Axe of Kolt!" Billy laughs and replies, "Give over! If that were true, it'd mean Magor is over 200 years old! He might be getting on a bit, but he's never that old! He still manages to chase the serving girls around when he comes down here for a drink! Mind you, I suppose he could've prolonged his life by arcane means, but not for THAT long!"

The conversation turns to other events which don't interest you. Pondering for a while on what has been said, you resolve to visit this sorcerer Magor first thing tomorrow morning. If you could find the whereabouts of the tomb of Kolt and recover this axe, you could make your fortune, as well as saving these good people from a hideous fate.

You retire to the room set aside for you by the innkeeper, and sleep soundly. After breaking your fast, you leave the inn early on Monday morning, ready to go up to Magor's tower.

By Inn
You are standing on the west side of the village green, by the large building, which a sign hanging from the wall by the door declares itself to be the "Dragonslayer's Arms" inn. The inn door leads In, going North takes you to the entrance to the inn yard and you can go South back along the track to the road. The village green itself lies to the East, SE and NE.

> e
You move east.

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.

> n
You move north.

North Side of Village Green
You are on the north side of the village green, where a wide track leads North towards the mountains,leading between the cottages which stand in clusters to the NW, NE and East. You can also go West, South, SE and SW across the green from here.

> n
You move North.

You walk north from the village past the cottages into farmland that soon gives way to open countryside that starts to rise as you get further away from the village. You are now in the foothills of the Droomdark mountains.

As you walk, you think about the outlaws that infest the forest east of Hengemire, and wonder if Magor can do anything about them? You resolve to tell Magor about the outlaws when you talk to him.

Following the path into the foothills, you eventually reach a junction where the track divides, the left hand branch heading towards a canyon, while the right hand one continues up towards the mountains themselves.

Mountain Track
You're on a track that zigzags up and down the rough scree-covered slope of the mountain. A trail leads off northwest towards a canyon, and the track continues to wind Up the mountain, entering the snow several hundred metres above. You have an excellent view of Hengemire village to the South.

> nw
You move northwest.

Entrance to Canyon
You're near the entrance to a narrow canyon in the mountains. You see that the canyon leads to a rocky outcrop at the western end on which stands a tall, slender tower. You can go West to the tower or SE back to the junction in the track.

> w
You move west.

By Tower
The canyon opens out to the top of a rocky outcrop overlooking the surrounding countryside. Perched about 3 metres from the edge of the outcrop is the tall tower, which soars above you for at least 50 metres. A small bell hangs from a metal bracket beside a large circular slab of rock which covers the entrance to the tower.

> replace clapper
You replace the clapper inside the bell to repair it.

> ring bell
Ding-a-ling! You wait a minute or two but you get no answer - maybe you should try again?

> ring bell
Ding-a-ling! Still no answer - perhaps one more try?

> ring bell
Ding-a-ling!

On the third ring you hear an exclamation from above you and look up to see a man's head, wearing a tall, pointed hat, looking down at you from a window high in the tower. You guess that it is Magor the sorcerer.

"I thought I heard the bell - someone's found the clapper and fixed it!" Magor exclaims. "Good grief, we've got a visitor, Akhenaten," he says to someone inside the tower. "Come on up," he calls to you. "I'll open the door!"

With that the rock slab rolls ponderously to one side to reveal a round opening leading West into the tower.

By Tower
The canyon opens out to the top of a rocky outcrop overlooking the surrounding countryside. Perched about 3 metres from the edge of the outcrop is the tall tower, which soars above you for at least 50 metres. The slab has rolled to one side to reveal a round opening leading West into the foot of the tower. A small bell hangs from a metal bracket beside the entrance.

> w
You move west.

Foot of Stairway
You're at the foot of some worn steps that spiral up through the solid rock. The round opening to the tower is open and leads east.

As you enter the tower, the hairs on the back of your neck stand on end as a voice speaks to you from the walls themselves!

"Welcome to my humble abode. Please come up the stairway and do not be alarmed by what you see when you get to the top. I have put various enchantments on the tower to make it more comfortable and suitable to my needs. By the way, watch out for the fourth step from the top, it's a bit loose."

> u
You walk up the spiral stairway to Magor's chamber. As you get higher you notice that the stairway doesn't get narrower as it should do in a normal tapering tower. Heeding his warning, you step over the fourth step from the top and then you enter the sorcerer's chamber.....

Magor's Chamber
You're in the main chamber of Magor's tower, a smoky, dark-cornered room that is full of mostly incomprehensible things. There are hundreds of books and scrolls in piles and on shelves, and on a long table by one wall, a strange thaumaturgical apparatus bubbles and seethes away.  Magor himself regards you from a high-backed chair next to the fire that blazes in a huge fireplace.  Perched on the back of Magor's chair is a large snowy owl, its huge golden eyes regarding you balefully. There is another chair similar to Magor's on the opposite side of the fireplace. While there are other doors and staircases leading off this chamber, the only exit you can take is Down.

As you glance around, you can see what Magor meant by "various enchantments" - his chamber is far bigger than what the tower looked like from outside.

Magor smiles at you and bids you sit down, which you do. "Well, young man, to what do we owe the pleasure of this visit? Tell me who you are first of all."

> say alaric to magor
You greet Magor and tell him that your name is Alaric Blackmoon. He asks you where you are from and you tell him a little about your past.

"You have obviously led an interesting and eventful life, Alaric. Now, please tell me why you have visited me?"

> tell magor about xixon
You tell Magor that the Xixon have invaded Hecate and Domreil is under siege.

Magor reacts with horror at your news. "Ye Gods!" he exclaims. "I thought the Xixon had been wiped out by King Kolt with the axe that my father forged from elfmetal. Some must have escaped and now they have returned to wreak their revenge!"

You tell Magor that King Kelson has issued a plea for anyone who knows where Kolt's tomb is and that you heard that Magor might know where it is? You add that you want to recover the axe and try to restore it to King Kelson so he can lead the fight to drive out the Xixon once again.

"Yes, I know where the tomb is, my father told me shortly before he died," Magor tells you. He ponders for a minute or so before continuing. You get the distinct impression that whatever he is going to say next you are not going to like very much!

"Very well, I will tell you where the tomb is, but first you must fulfill a quest for me," he tells you. You close your eyes and sigh - you knew there was going to be a catch!

"On the far side of the river Sutlej lies Direwood Forest. This is the domain of the sorceress Galhexia. Many years ago she stole a magical locus from me known as the Evil Orb of Allinor. She has been using this locus in her quest for immortality. She has sacrificed hundreds of innocent people in pursuit of her goal and must be stopped. You must kill Galhexia so that I am able to venture into the forest to recover the Orb!"

You are momentarily stunned by this request, but you realise that recovering this orb for Magor is the only way you will learn the location of Kolt's tomb. You tell Magor you will accept his challenge, but you are penniless and need funds in order to equip yourself for the quest.

He snaps his fingers and a pouch magically appears in his hand. He tosses the pouch to you and you catch it. It chinks with the sound of coins.

"That pouch contains all the gold coins that I can spare at the moment," he tells you. "Use it carefully to equip yourself for your quest." As you tie the pouch to your belt he gestures at it and you feel a tingling sensation in your belly. "I have put a spell on the pouch which will stop anyone apart from yourself trying to remove it from your belt," he tells you. "Now, have you any questions you would like to ask me?"

> tell magor about outlaws
You tell Magor about the outlaws in the forest.

"Are they still there?" he asks in a surprised tone. "I thought the garrison at Woolwych would've sent some troops out to deal with them by now!"

He turns round and looks at the owl perched on the back of his chair.

"Akhenaten," he says pleasantly to the owl. "Be a good chap and fly over to Major Prune at the Hussar's barracks in Woolwych."

The owl regards him balefully as he continues: "Tell him if he doesn't get a squadron of his men down to the forest to deal with those outlaws pretty quickly, I will go over there and turn him into a toad - again!"

The owl bobs his head in acknowledgement and hops onto the nearest windowsill and, spreading his impressive wings, swoops off in a northerly direction towards Woolwych.

Magor's Chamber
You're in the main chamber of Magor's tower, a smoky, dark-cornered room that is full of mostly incomprehensible things. There are hundreds of books and scrolls in piles and on shelves, and on a long table by one wall, a strange thaumaturgical apparatus bubbles and seethes away.  Magor himself regards you from a high-backed chair next to the fire that blazes in a huge fireplace.  There is another chair similar to Magor's on the opposite side of the fireplace. While there are other doors and staircases leading off this chamber, the only exit you can take is Down.

> ask magor about axe
You ask Magor about the Axe of Kolt.

"Although I would like to lay claim to the credit, it was my father - also called Magor - who forged the Axe of Kolt," Magor tells you with a far-away look in his eyes. "He journeyed far around the world, across land, sea, desert and mountain, to the legendary lands where the elves live in their hidden valleys. He came back with enough elfmetal to make a double-headed axe which, when it was being forged, had to be infused with the blood of the person who would wield it, King Kolt. Powerful enchantments were then cast upon the axe so that the slightest scratch would mean death to any Xixon. The axe would also emit a deafening note which can only be heard by any Xixon. However, the axe would only have these powers when wielded by Kolt or any of his direct descendants - in anyone else's hands it it is just an ordinary axe."

> ask magor about tomb
You ask Magor if he can tell you anything about the tomb?

"Kolt's tomb was designed to deter looters," Magor tells you. "If you should find it, I would advise you to be extremely careful when you approach it, there will be traps set to catch out the unwary."

> ask magor about evil orb
You ask Magor about the Evil Orb of Allinor.

"The Evil Orb is one of a pair," Magor tells you, walking over to a pedestal you have not noticed before, the top of which is covered with a black cloth. "This is the Good Orb of Allinor," he says, lifting the cloth to reveal a clear glass ball within which bright lights swirl and glitter. You stare at the orb, mesmerised by the kaleidoscopic display, until Magor re-covers the orb and you snap out of your trance.

"Together the orbs are known as 'The Twin Orbs of Allinor'," Magor informs you. "They were created a millennia ago by my many-times Great-Grandfather Allinor the Great. He was one of the most powerful wizards of all time and legend has that he had only intended to create one orb, which would act as a focus into the magical dimensions. However, as the orb was created, another appeared next to it but this orb seethed with dark forces and Allinor realised immediately that it was the opposite of the first orb, one that would see into the dark dimensions."

You ask Magor what became of the dark orb.

"It was kept locked away deep within the Earth for hundreds of years, its location being kept secret by the descendants of Allinor until about a decade ago when it was stolen from its hiding place by the sorceress Galhexia. She has been using it to try to gain immortality, but so far that has eluded her. I would attempt to recover the orb myself, but she always knows when I am near and her magic is too powerful - it would be instant death for me if ever I came within her sight."

> ask magor about Galhexia
Magor's eyes look sadly at you.

"Galhexia was once a very highly respected sorceress," he tells you. "Sadly, she started dabbling in the dark side of magic and she stole the Evil Orb of Allinor from its repository deep under the earth. Her quest for immortality turned into an obsession and now it has taken her over completely, and she is totally evil. If I were powerful enough, I would attempt to kill her - even though she is my own twin sister!"

> ask magor about good orb
You ask Magor about the Good Orb of Allinor.

"The Good Orb is one of a pair," Magor tells you, walking over to a pedestal you have not noticed before, the top of which is covered with a black cloth. "This is the Good Orb of Allinor," he says, lifting the cloth to reveal a clear glass ball about 10 cm in diameter within which bright lights swirl and glitter. You stare at the orb, mesmerised by the kaleidoscopic display, until Magor re-covers the orb and you snap out of your trance.

"Together the orbs are known as 'The Twin Orbs of Allinor'," Magor informs you. "They were created a millennia ago by my many-times Great-Grandfather Allinor the Great. He was one of the most powerful wizards of all time and legend has that he had only intended to create one orb, which would act as a focus into the magical dimensions. However, as the orb was created, another appeared next to it but that orb seethed with dark forces and Allinor realised immediately that it was the opposite of the first orb, one that would see into the dark dimensions."

You ask Magor how come he has the good orb.

"My family have always been custodians of the Good Orb," he tells you. "It is safe in our possession."

> ask magor about apparatus
You ask Magor about his thaumaturgical apparatus.

"Ah, you noticed that, did you?" the sorcerer says, a sly grin appearing on his face. "Just distilling myself a drop of whiskey - purely for medicinal purposes, you understand!"

> ask magor about whiskey
You ask Magor about the whiskey he is distilling.

"It's a blend I discovered a few decades ago," the sorcerer tells you. "A glass a day keeps the chills away!"

"Hmmphh!" you think to yourself - more like a bottle a day!

> d
You take your leave of Magor, thanking him for his help.

"Good luck with your quest!" he tells you.

You walk down the stairway, nearly falling down as you forget about the wonky step, and leave the tower.

By Tower
The canyon opens out to the top of a rocky outcrop overlooking the surrounding countryside. Perched about 3 metres from the edge of the outcrop is the tall tower, which soars above you for at least 50 metres. A small bell hangs from a metal bracket beside a large circular slab of rock which covers the entrance to the tower.

> e
You move east.

Entrance to Canyon
You're near the entrance to a narrow canyon in the mountains. You see that the canyon leads to a rocky outcrop at the western end on which stands a tall, slender tower. You can go West to the tower or SE back to the junction in the track.

> se
You move southeast.

Mountain Track
You're on a track that zigzags up and down the rough scree-covered slope of the mountain. A trail leads off northwest towards a canyon, and the track continues to wind Up the mountain, entering the snow several hundred metres above. You have an excellent view of Hengemire village to the South.

> s
You walk down the track back to Hengemire. When you arrive at the village green, you see it is now populated with many traders setting up their stalls for the market.....

North Side of Village Green
You are on the north side of the village green, where a wide track leads North towards the mountains,leading between the cottages which stand in clusters to the NW, NE and East. You can also go West, South, SE and SW across the green from here.  The green is covered with carts and other wheeled vehicles which belong to the traders who have come for the market. The traders themselves are busy erecting their stalls and laying out the displays of their goods for when they start trading once the market is open.

> s
You move south.

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.  All around you the green is covered with carts and other wheeled vehicles which belong to the traders who have come for the market. The traders themselves are busy erecting their stalls and laying out the displays of their goods for when they start trading once the market is open.

> talk to traders
The traders are too busy setting up their stalls to talk to you. One or two tell you to "Go away!", thinking you are a beggar.

One old lady who is walking across the green is more helpful when she hears the traders being rude to you.

"Why don't you go and have a drink in the inn while this lot set their stalls up?" she suggests. "They'll be at least another hour before they are ready."

You thank the lady for her suggestion. She smiles at you and hurries on her way.

> w
You move west.

By Inn
You are standing on the west side of the village green, by the large building, which a sign hanging from the wall by the door declares itself to be the "Dragonslayer's Arms" inn. The inn door leads In, going North takes you to the entrance to the inn yard and you can go South back along the track to the road. The village green itself lies to the East, SE and NE.  Over on the green you see it is covered with carts and other wheeled vehicles which belong to the traders who have come for the market. The traders themselves are busy erecting their stalls and laying out the displays of their goods.

> in
You move in.

East End of Inn
You are in the main room of the Dragonslayer's Arms inn. It is a large, dark room with a low, beamed ceiling and a stone floor strewn with rushes. Tallow candles gutter on several tables and on various places around the inn. The room smells of wine and ale, but it seems to be well-kept. Against the north wall are a row of barrels on trestles, in front of which is a plank of wood, supported by two tables, which is known as the "bar". The room extends West and the door leads Out.  There are a few people in the inn, mostly traders and a few villagers waiting for the market to open.  Sarah Ann Roffey is here.

> wait
You wait for a while but then decide to buy a tankard of ale, costing you one gold coin, from Sarah Ann and you sit quietly thinking about the quest that Magor has asked you to embark on, wondering what dangers you will face in Direwood forest and beyond.

After an hour or so, you hear a bell ring outside and everyone in the inn downs their drinks and walks out. You assume the market is open so you finish your own drink, bid farewell to Sarah Ann, who blows you a cheeky kiss, and you walk out of the inn.....

By Inn
You are standing on the west side of the village green, by the large building, which a sign hanging from the wall by the door declares itself to be the "Dragonslayer's Arms" inn. The inn door leads In, going North takes you to the entrance to the inn yard and you can go South back along the track to the road. The village green itself lies to the East, SE and NE.  The market is now in full swing over on the village green and the noise of the traders yelling out their spiel is deafening.

> s
You move south.

SW Side of Village Green
You are on the southwest side of the village green, by the road that runs through Hengemire, which lies South and SE of where you stand. A rutted dirt track runs roughly North along the edge of the green to the Inn, and you can go East or NE onto the main part of the green.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. The trapper is here, standing sullenly in front of a huge pile of furs.

> say hello to trapper
You say a cheery "Hello!" to the trapper. The man gives a barely perceptible nod of his head and glowers at you from under his wild mane of hair. If he said anything in greeting at all, it was lost in the cacophony around you.

> ask trapper about dwark
You ask the trapper about the creature he encountered in the mountain pass.

"Nearly 'ad me, it did," he tells you, eager to retell his experience. "It might be almost blind but it could sense me by my body heat. Only reason I managed to escape was because I tripped over as I was running away from it and fell into a snowdrift! The cold snow hid me from it. I realised it couldn't sense me, so waited until it had moved down the pass then I legged it, took shelter in a little cave I often use to sleep in at the eastern end of the pass."

You thank the trapper for telling you his story - what useful information to have!

> ask trapper about cave
You ask the trapper about the cave in the mountain pass.

"Oh arr, it's cave I use when I'm trapping up in the mountains," he tells you. "Snug an' warm it be, being sheltered from the winds from north 'n' east like it is. I dare say other folks use it from time to time, someone replaced my furs not so long ago - I dunno why, they were only 10 year old!"

You thank the trapper for telling you about the cave - what useful information to have!

> buy fur
You rummage through the pile of furs, trying on a few, until you find one that fits and is thick enough.

You offer the trapper two gold coins for the fur coat. He goes into a fake choking fit and splutters, "WHAT! Don't insult me mate, that's worth at least 10 gold coins! What would my poor old missis say if I let it go for two - she spent hours sewing that coat!"

You haggle furiously with the trapper for several minutes, drawing a crowd of onlookers who love to see someone driving such a hard bargain.

Eventually, after telling a sob story that left the trapper completely unmoved, you just happen to drop Magor's name into the proceedings. His manner changes completely.

"Well, seeing 'as you's a mate of the old wizard, I'm willing to let it go for 5 gold coins, not a penny less!"

You are, however, not to be robbed, so you haggle a bit more and manage to knock the price down to 4 gold coins. You hand over the coins to a cheer from the onlookers, while the trapper looks at you rather crestfallen that he has let the coat go for so little.

As you walk away, however, you notice that a lot of people are now rummaging through the pile of furs and haggling with the trapper in the hope of getting a similar bargain.

> n
You move north.

By Inn
You are standing on the west side of the village green, by the large building, which a sign hanging from the wall by the door declares itself to be the "Dragonslayer's Arms" inn. The inn door leads In, going North takes you to the entrance to the inn yard and you can go South back along the track to the road. The village green itself lies to the East, SE and NE.  The market is now in full swing over on the village green and the noise of the traders yelling out their spiel is deafening.

> ne
You move northeast.

North Side of Village Green
You are on the north side of the village green, where a wide track leads North towards the mountains,leading between the cottages which stand in clusters to the NW, NE and East. You can also go West, South, SE and SW across the green from here.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. There is a lampmaker's stall here.

> talk to lampmaker
You greet the lampmaker and he pauses from yelling out his spiel and replies,

"Good day to you sir. As you can see, I have lamps at very affordable prices."

While he waits for you to tell him that you want to buy a lamp, he resumes his spiel again.

> buy oil lamp
You tell the lampmaker that you need to buy a lamp to light your way through rough terrain.

"I have good sturdy lamps that can take rough treatment," he explains. "The standard model, my best-selling lamp, is three gold coins."

You hand over three of Magor's gold coins and the lampmaker tells you to take your pick of the standard model lamps, which you do.

"Will you be needing to buy something to light the lamp with?" the lampmaker asks you. "I have an ingenious little lamplighter of my own design which will enable you to light the lamp without burning you fingers. It only costs one gold coin."

The lampmaker continues to yell out his spiel as he waits for you to make your mind up.

> buy lamplighter
You tell the lampmaker that you will buy a lamplighter.

"A wise decision sir," he tells you, handing over one of his little devices as you hand him one gold coin.

He points at the lamp you just bought from him.

"If you want some oil for the lamp, wait by the stone cross," he tells you. "The oilman will be along soon, he will fill your lamp for you."

> s
You move south.

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A stall selling all sorts of armour stands here, the armourer is sitting by the side of the stall working on an armoured gauntlet.

> x cross
A tall, weather-worn stone cross. On one side of the square base is an inscription.

> read inscription
The worn inscription reads:

In Memory of The Men of Hengemire Who Died in the Xixon War 3740 - 3745

Their Sacrifice Will Never Be Forgotten

R.I.P.

> wait
You wait for a while, watching the goings-on in the market.

At one point a thief runs towards you, chased by an irate trader. You stick out a foot and trip the thief, who falls sprawling onto the ground. The trader grabs him, takes back the stolen goods and hands the miscreant over to a market beadle who roughly frog-marches him away to face justice.

Eventually the oilman comes ambling by, calling out to anyone who wants to buy oil for their lamps.....

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A stall selling all sorts of armour stands here, the armourer is sitting by the side of the stall working on an armoured gauntlet.  The oilman is here.

> talk to oilman
I don't understand what you want to do with the armourer.

> buy oil
You tell the oilman you would like to buy some oil and you hand over one gold coin.

Opening the valve of his bladder, he fills the tank of your lamp with oil. You thank him and he serves a number of people before moving on.....

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A stall selling all sorts of armour stands here, the armourer is sitting by the side of the stall working on an armoured gauntlet.

> n
You move north.

North Side of Village Green
You are on the north side of the village green, where a wide track leads North towards the mountains,leading between the cottages which stand in clusters to the NW, NE and East. You can also go West, South, SE and SW across the green from here.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. There is a lampmaker's stall here.

> n
You move north.

Mountain Track
You're on a track that zigzags up and down the rough scree-covered slope of the mountain. A trail leads off northwest towards a canyon, and the track continues to wind Up the mountain, entering the snow several hundred metres above. You have an excellent view of Hengemire village to the South.

> light lamp
You turn the knob on the side of the lamp, then you light the wick of the lamp with your lamplighter. The lamp begins to shine with a clear bright light.

> wear fur
Ok, you put on the fur coat.

> u

You start your trek up the mountain. At first it is easy going but soon it gets harder and steeper. It also takes longer than you expected and after a few hours darkness falls.

The last stretch up to the entrance to the pass is over a steep scree-covered slope and you slip and slide down a couple metres more than once. You think to yourself that it would be very dangerous to attempt a descent back down even in fair weather in the daytime - at night in these conditions it would be suicidal!

Eventually you make it safely to the entrance to the pass.....

Entrance to Pass
You are at the entrance to a narrow pass leading East between two peaks of the mountains. Through the swirling snow you can see that this is the only way you can go other than back Down the mountain. However, you think that going back down might be rather dangerous in the dark. Through the swirling snow you can the glimmer of lights in Hengemire village far below.

> e
You move east.

Near West End of Pass
You are near the west end of the pass, the entrance being about 300 metres to the West. The pass, which continues East, is about 20 metres wide here and through the swirling snow you can just see the walls either side of you disappear into the darkness beyond the light from your lamp. There is a thick layer of snow covering the ground and deep drifts up against the sides of the pass either side of you.

Suddenly, above the noise of the wind and swirling snow, you hear a howl echo along the pass. Is the creature that made the sound the dreaded dwark?

> e
You move east.

In Mountain Pass
You are in the pass that runs east-west through the mountains. The pass is about 15 metres wide at this point and the walls either side of you vanish into the darkness beyond the light from your lamp. A deep drift of snow has piled up against the side of the pass here.

You hear a wild scream and ahead of you to the east a large creature comes towards you out of the snowstorm, its head questing from side to side as it tries to detect the body heat of any potential prey - this means you!

> dive in snow
You throw yourself into the deep snowdrift at the side of the pass.....

Buried in Snowdrift
You are buried in a snowdrift at the side of the pass. The only way you can go is Up or Out into the pass again.

You hear the dwark roar in frustration in the pass above you as its feeble mind tries to work out where its prey has gone. The creature stomps off along the pass to the west.

> u
You scramble out of the snowdrift into the pass.

In Mountain Pass
You are in the pass that runs east-west through the mountains. The pass is about 15 metres wide at this point and the walls either side of you vanish into the darkness beyond the light from your lamp. A deep drift of snow has piled up against the side of the pass here.

The Dwark screams in rage, the noise of its roar reverberating off the walls of the pass, making you wince in pain as the sound batters your ears!

You had better move away from here in case the Dwark comes back.

> e
You move east along the pass - but the Dwark is not far behind you!

In Mountain Pass
You are in the pass that runs through the mountains where the pass bends to the SE. The pass is about 20 metres wide here and the walls either side of you rise unseen into the darkness beyond the light from your lamp. There is a layer of snow covering the ground and a deep drift up against the side of the pass here.

You glance behind you and see the dwark entering the pool of light cast by your lantern - you only have seconds to make your next move!

> dive in snow
You again throw yourself into the deep snowdrift at one side of the pass.....

Buried in Snowdrift
You are buried in a snowdrift at the side of the pass. The only way you can go is Up into the pass again.

As you burrow down into the snowdrift to escape from the dwark, your hand closes upon a small rock.

You hear the dwark scream again and the sound of it digging in the snow - it has worked out where you are hiding and is trying to dig you out!

> u
You scramble out of the snowdrift into the pass.

In Mountain Pass
You are in the pass that runs through the mountains where the pass bends to the SE. The pass is about 20 metres wide here and the walls either side of you rise unseen into the darkness beyond the light from your lamp. There is a layer of snow covering the ground and a deep drift up against the side of the pass here.

You emerge from the snowdrift to find the dwark is right next to you! The creature screams in triumph and raises its arms so it can slash down at you with its sabre-like claws!

> throw rock at dwark
You hurl the rock at the dwark's head with all your might and it hits the creature's head directly on the heat-sensing organ above its eyes.

The effect is dramatic as the creature screams in agony and it staggers back in pain, shaking its head from side to side. The ground shakes as the dwark falls to the ground, momentarily stunned - now is your chance to get away if you are quick enough!

> run se
You run along the pass as quickly as you can in the snow. Behind you the dwark has recovered from being hit by the rock that you threw at it and the enraged animal is coming after you, its roars of rage echoing along the pass. After a couple of minutes you reach a bend in the pass.....

Bend in Pass
You are at a bend in the pass where it goes northwest and east. The snow is deeper here and it is making the going harder.

The dwark, with its longer legs and rage-heightened strength, is catching up to you - it will catch you up if you don't hurry!

> run e
You run east along the pass with the enraged dwark only metres behind you, its roars of rage resounding off the walls of the pass so that you are running into a cacophony of sound that batters your eardrums.

Exhaustion is beginning to tell and as you think the beast is going to catch you, you see sharp bend ahead of you and, in the far wall of the pass, a small black circle that must be the entrance to the cave the trapper told you about. You hurl yourself towards it and, with the dwark slashing at your heels in order to prevent your escape, you find yourself in a narrow tunnel which you scramble along before tumbling into a larger space at the end. To your surprise you land on something soft, but the dwark has thrust its long arm into the tunnel and its sabre-taloned paws are trying to scoop you out, so you press yourself against the far wall of the cave out of its reach.....

In Small Cave
You are in a small cave in the side of the mountain. A short tunnel just big enough for a man to crawl through leads Out to the mountain pass. A pile of furs on the floor of the cave indicates it has been used by people as a refuge in the recent past.

As you crouch at the back of the cave, the dwark's claws scythe through the air mere centimetres from you, its screams of rage and frustration filling the cave with a wall of sound and you clamp your hands over your ears to prevent your eardrums from bursting.

After what seems like an eternity, the dwark gives up its efforts to reach you and, giving vent to one last scream of rage, it withdraws its arm and you hear it stomp off along the pass in frustration.

You collapse onto the floor which is covered in a pile of old furs and you fall into an instant exhausted sleep.

In Small Cave
You are in a small cave in the side of the mountain. A short tunnel just big enough for a man to crawl through leads Out to the mountain pass. A pile of furs on the floor of the cave indicates it has been used by people as a refuge in the recent past.  Also here is a lit oil lamp.

You are woken next morning by the sound of bird song and slowly open your eyes to see a robin perched on the toe of your boot. The bird chirrups at you as if to say "What are you doing in my cave?" before taking flight out of the cave like a red and brown dart.

> get lamp
Ok, you pick up the lit oil lamp.

> extinguish lamp
You extinguish the lamp by turning the knob on the side.

> out
You move out.

East End of Pass
You are outside the cave at the eastern end of the pass through the mountains. Daylight reveals that the pass itself is completely blocked by snow and thus the only way you can go is Down the mountain via a track. From up here you have a commanding view of the land to the south.

> d

You walk down the track, taking your time and taking in the view of the surrounding countryside. It takes you some time to make the descent and it is mid-morning before you reach the road at the end of the path.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.

> e
You move east.

Junction in Road
You are at a junction in the East-West road, where another road goes South towards the river Sutlej, entering a small village that nestles on the bank of the river. A wide lane leads off NE through the trees and you can see a column of smoke rising from a chimney in the gaps between the branches in that direction. By the side of the road here there is a triple-armed signpost.

> s
You move south.

Road through Village
You are on a road that runs North-South through a sleepy little village towards the river further south. Here you see several cottages and larger houses that sit in neatly-tended gardens, the nearest one being accessible via a gate which is to the East. On the west side of the road is a large white-washed cottage with a sign above the door which reads "Village Store". The door leading in to the store is closed and a hand-written notice has been nailed to it which reads "Gone to Hengemire Market - Back later".

> e
You move east.

In Garden of Cottage
You are in the garden of the cottage on a path that winds through neat little flower beds to a yellow-painted door. By the door against the wall of the cottage there is a wooden bench.  Sitting on the bench here is a little old lady, she is shivering with cold.

The elderly lady looks up as you approach and smiles at you. "Hello young man," she says to you. "My name is Edwina. Can you please help me? I have lost my door key in one of my flower beds and I'm locked out."

> say hello
You greet Edwina and tell her your name.

"Hello young Alaric," she replies, "Can you please help me find my key?"

> ask about key
(Edwina)

You ask Edwina about her door key.

"I must have dropped it when I was weeding the earth around my plants and then I trod it under the surface afterwards," she tells you. "I ought to keep a spare hidden somewhere but I would probably forget where I hid it!"

You tell Edwina that you will help her find her lost key.

"That is very kind of you, young man," she tells you.

You start to search the dirt in her flower beds by hand but she stops you.

"It will take you all day to find the key that way," she tells you. "If you can find a sieve it will be much quicker. Alas, the key to my shed is in my cottage, so you cannot use that one.

You ask Edwina where you might find a sieve?

"You could try the farmyard on the road to Hengemire," she tells you. "I'm sure Farmer Feighan will lend you one."

> say to edwina are you cold
You ask Edwina if she is feeling cold?

"Yes I am," she tells you. "If I have to stay out in the cold much longer I will catch a cold!"

You gallantly tell the lady that she can wear your fur coat. She accepts delightedly and you take off your fur coat and hold it out for the old lady to wear. She slips her arms into the sleeves and pulls it around her - it is far too big for her but that doesn't matter. She sits back down on the bench looking snug and warm.

> w
You leave Edwina and walk out of her garden.

"Thank you for offering to find my key!" she calls after you. "And also for lending me your coat, it's ever so warm!"

Road through Village
You are on a road that runs North-South through a sleepy little village towards the river further south. Here you see several cottages and larger houses that sit in neatly-tended gardens, the nearest one being accessible via a gate which is to the East. On the west side of the road is a large white-washed cottage with a sign above the door which reads "Village Store". The door leading in to the store is closed and a hand-written notice has been nailed to it which reads "Gone to Hengemire Market - Back later".

> s
You move south.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

> search leaves
You search through the pile of leaves and, to your delight, at the bottom you find a rather grubby gold coin which someone must have dropped. You quickly wipe it clean on your trousers and slip it into the leather pouch that Magor gave you before anyone notices and can lay claim to it.

> s
You move south.

On River Bank
You are on the south bank of the river Sutlej, where a path runs East-West along the bank as far as the eye can see. Here a jetty juts out into the river which you can get on to by going South. Across the river you can see Direwood forest on the far shore with the black mass of cloud looming above it.  Pulled up onto the bank of the river here is a ferryboat.

> s
You move south.

On Jetty
You are on the jetty which projects out from the bank into the river Sutlej. If there was a boat moored here you could walk Down the steps into it, but as there isn't the only way you can go is North onto the river bank. Sitting here, gazing wistfully out at the river, is the ferryman.

> say hello to ferryman
You say hello to the ferryman and that you want to cross the river to Hecate. He looks at you and replies,

"I don't know why you wanna go across to there, we've spotted Xixon on the riverbank and that sorceress controls the heart of the forest," he says in astonishment. "In any case, my boat has sprung a leak and I can't take anyone anywhere until I can get it repaired."

You tell Denny that you need to get across to Hecate so you can search for the lost Axe of Kolt.

"Rather you than me," he tells you, looking you up and down, noting your lack of weapons and protection. "If I were going across there I would make sure I was armed to the teeth and wearing some sturdy chainmail!"

You tell Denny that you do not have the money to buy any weapons.

"Well, at least get yourself some chainmail!" he warns you.

> ask about boat
(Denny Joyce)

You ask the ferryman what happened to his boat.

"We struck a tree trunk that was floating downstream after a storm must'a uprooted it," he tells you. "It made a hole as big as a dustbin lid! I need some decent wood to fix it but I can't afford to buy any at the moment."

> say i want to cross river
(to Denny Joyce)

He ignores you.

> say mend boat
(to Denny Joyce)

You tell the ferryman that you will get the wood to repair his boat if he will take you across the river. He immediately brightens up and replies,

"I would be most grateful if you can do that for me, kind sir," he says in astonishment. "I will of course sail you across the river once my boat is repaired."

> n
You move north.

On River Bank
You are on the south bank of the river Sutlej, where a path runs East-West along the bank as far as the eye can see. Here a jetty juts out into the river which you can get on to by going South. Across the river you can see Direwood forest on the far shore with the black mass of cloud looming above it.  Pulled up onto the bank of the river here is a ferryboat.

> n
You move north.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

Junction in Road
You are at a junction in the East-West road, where another road goes South towards the river Sutlej, entering a small village that nestles on the bank of the river. A wide lane leads off NE through the trees and you can see a column of smoke rising from a chimney in the gaps between the branches in that direction. By the side of the road here there is a triple-armed signpost.

> w
You move west.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.

> w
You move west.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road and to the north the mountains thrust above them into the sky. Gaps in the hedgerow lead North to a farmyard and South to a sawmill.

> s
You move south.

By Sawmill
You are outside a sawmill which stands on the bank of the fast-flowing river that runs down to the Sutlej river. The road is to the North.  There is silence from the sawmill and there doesn't seem to be any wood being sawn at the moment.  The sawyer is here.

The sawyer is looking most dejected and you notice he is holding a long piece of metal in his hand.

"I'm afraid if you are here to ask me to cut some wood, you are out of luck," he says holding up the piece of metal, which you now notice is bent. "This connecting rod from my saw machinery has bent and now I cannot cut any wood."

> say hello to sawyer
You greet the sawyer and tell him who you are. You then tell him how sorry you are that his machinery is not working.

"I need some wood to help the ferryman fix his boat," you tell the sawyer.

"I wish I could help," he tells you. "Until I get this connecting rod straightened any wood we cut will have to be done by hand and that takes much longer."

> ask about rod
(the sawyer)

You ask the sawyer how the rod got bent.

"A bolt sheared in the mechanism," he tells you. "That in turn caused the rod to bend. I have a spare bolt but not a spare rod."

> take rod
You take the bent rod from the sawyer - it is surprisingly heavy.

"If I straighten this rod for you, will you cut some wood for me?" you ask the sawyer.

"Most certainly!" he replies happily. "I will cut whatever wood you need. Well, I have some other jobs to be getting on with so I'll see you back here later on then?"

The sawyer nods in farewell and walks away into his sawmill.

By Sawmill
You are outside a sawmill which stands on the bank of the fast-flowing river that runs down to the Sutlej river. The road is to the North.  There is silence from the sawmill and there doesn't seem to be any wood being sawn at the moment.

> n
You move north.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road and to the north the mountains thrust above them into the sky. Gaps in the hedgerow lead North to a farmyard and South to a sawmill.

> n
You move north.

In Farmyard
You are in the cobble-stoned yard of a small farm, which is enclosed on three sides by farm buildings. A farmhouse lies on the west side with a tall barn to the north, while the east side is made up of a row of stables and byres. Beyond the barn and the stables you see a field with various farm animals grazing in it. The road is to the South through a gap in the hedgerow.

You hear a bark from inside the farmhouse and the collie dog appears at the door and sees you. You are about to take to your heels when you hear a voice snap out "Down Gyp!". The dog immediately lays down in the doorway of the farmhouse and a man walks out of the farmhouse and regards you warily.

"Hello, I'm farmer Feighan," he informs you before asking, "What brings you to my farm, you looking for work?"

You tell the farmer who you are and that you are seeking to borrow a sieve in order to find the key for the old lady. The farmer considers your request for a minute or two before replying.

"Yes, most certainly Alaric, but first you must do me a service in return," he tells you, and he points to a pile of logs you had not noticed before. "You chop that lot into firewood for me and I will lend you a sieve. Problem is that my axe is broken so you will have to find your own from somewhere."

With that, he turns and walks inside the farmhouse, closely followed by Gyp, and closes the door, leaving you standing there wondering where you are going to get an axe from.....

In Farmyard
You are in the cobble-stoned yard of a small farm, which is enclosed on three sides by farm buildings. A farmhouse lies on the west side with a tall barn to the north, while the east side is made up of a row of stables and byres. Beyond the barn and the stables you see a field with various farm animals grazing in it. The road is to the South through a gap in the hedgerow.  Piled high here are some short logs.

> s
You move south.

Junction in Road
You are at a junction in the East-West road, where another road goes South towards the river Sutlej, entering a small village that nestles on the bank of the river. A wide lane leads off NE through the trees and you can see a column of smoke rising from a chimney in the gaps between the branches in that direction. By the side of the road here there is a triple-armed signpost.

> ne
You move northeast.

Outside Forge
The lane has led you to a blacksmith's forge, a low brick-built building with a slate roof that occupies a clearing in the woodland.  A pair of large wooden doors are open either side of a wide doorway that leads In to the forge. There is a large freshly painted sign above the doors of the forge.

> in
You move in.

Inside Forge
You stand inside the forge building, a dark-shadowed place smelling strongly of smoke and hot metal. It is dominated by the forge itself, the fire of which glows red hot in the darkness. The fire is being kept hot by the air blown into it by a large bellows which is being worked by the blacksmith's apprentice. The doors lead Out to the lane.  Standing here by his anvil, working some white hot metal, is the blacksmith George Steers.

> say hello to blacksmith
You say hello to the blacksmith and tell him your name.

"How do then, master Blackmoon, what service can I do for you?" he replies, mopping the sweat from his brow with a chequered handkerchief.

> say to blacksmith straighten rod
You ask the blacksmith if he will straighten the rod for you.

"Well, that won't take much effort," he says to you. "Tell ya what, you bring me a nice cool tankard of beer from the 'Ferryman Awaits' and I'll straighten the rod for you."

The blacksmith resumes working the metal on his anvil, muttering instructions to Willy as he does so, while you resign yourself to running yet another errand.

> out
You move out.

Outside Forge

Here you see several cottages and larger houses that sit in neatly-tended gardens, the nearest one being accessible via a gate which is to the East. Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

> in
You move in.

In Tavern
You are in the main room of "The Ferryman Awaits" tavern. In contrast to the inn at Hengemire, it is a dark, scruffy place that reeks of fish. The tavernkeeper is lounging in a chair in front of three large barrels of ale that rest on x-shaped trestles against the wall of the tavern opposite the door. Seated on benches around the one table the tavern boasts are a number of fishermen, who stare at you suspiciously.

> buy beer
You tell the tavern keeper you want a tankard of cold beer for the blacksmith and you offer him a gold coin for it.

"Sorry," he tells you apologetically. "A tankard of beer costs one silver coin and I'm afraid I've run out of change. I normally get some from Mistress Newman in the village store, but she is away at the market in Hengemire today."

> ask robert about roffey
You ask the tavernkeeper about the surname 'Roffey' as there seem to be lots of people called that around here.

"Yes, there are," he tells you. "The surname is very common in these parts. There's even a village called Roffey further to the west. They are all cousins to some degree, as the name goes back many generations."

> say to men cross river
You tell the men that you want someone to take you across the river to Hecate. They look at each other and then at you, and one of them replies,

"I don't know why you wanna go across to there, the place is crawling with the Xixon and that sorceress lives in the middle," he says in astonishment. "None of us is willing to risk it, if you sail too close when fishing the Xixon start to fire arrows at you."

> out
You move out.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

> n
You move north.
