East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.

You hear a noise behind you and realise it is the sound of many horses coming along the road from the east. Sure enough, a company of mounted soldiers comes trotting along, led by an officer on a red roan charger. The officer draws level with you and signals his men to stop. He dismounts from his horse and salutes you.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.  Major Prune is here, standing by his charger, with a squadron of mounted Hussars in a column behind him.

"Good day to you fellow," the officer says in a clipped tone. "I am Major Prune from the barracks at Woolwych. My men and I are seeking some outlaws hereabouts. Can you tell me where they are lurking?"

> say yes
(to Major Prune)

"Yes," you tell the Major, pointing towards the forest. "The outlaws are in the forest further west."

His face breaks into a grin and he salutes you again. "Thank you sir!" he tells you and, leaping up into the saddle of his charger, he signals to his men.

"OK lads, let's have some fun with these outlaws!" He spurs his horse into a gallop and the squadron rides off behind him towards the forest.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.

> w
You move west.

East-West Road

> w
You move west.

Bridge over River
You are on a bridge which crosses a narrow river that flows down from the mountains to join the Sutlej river further south. The forest is thinner here and you can see the edge of the forest further East where the road emerges into daylight. The road also goes SW deeper into the forest.

As you reach the bridge over the river you hear the sound of men fighting coming from the forest. From the noise you reckon that the Hussars are giving the outlaws a jolly good pasting!

After several more minutes in which the noise of the fighting diminishes then ceases altogether, the Hussars, led by a blood-splattered Major Prune, come riding out of the forest, herding the surviving outlaws before them.

A couple of bodies slung over the saddles of horses being led mean that the Hussars did not come out of the battle unscathed. You notice that one horse is piled high with the weapons taken from the outlaws.

As the column of riders and outlaws trudge past you, the Major halts beside you and throws a quick salute.

"Thanks for the information about the outlaws, here's a small reward," he says to you, taking a gold coin from his pocket and handing it to you. "We'll send some men with a wagon to remove the bodies of the outlaws we killed as soon as we get back."

Saluting once again, the Major wheels his charger and gallops off after his men. As you watch and put the gold coin into the leather pouch they all ride off along the road to the east then they are lost to view.

Bridge over River
You are on a bridge which crosses a narrow river that flows down from the mountains to join the Sutlej river further south. The forest is thinner here and you can see the edge of the forest further East where the road emerges into daylight. The road also goes SW deeper into the forest.

> sw
You move southwest.

Road through Forest
You are on the road from Hengemire in the depths of a dark forest. The canopy above you, although largely bare of leaves, is so thick it blots out most of the sunlight. The road goes West to Hengemire and bends to the NE as it goes deeper into the forest. Here is where the Hussars fought the outlaws in a pitched battle and the bodies of the outlaws that were killed lay in a row a few metres north of the road partly concealed from view by some bushes.

> w
You move west.

Road through Old Forest
You are just inside the forest on the road from Hengemire to Chaldon. To the West the road emerges from the trees while going East will take you deeper into the forest.

> w
You move west.

Road East of Hengemire
You are about 100 metres from where the road from Hengemire enters the Old Forest. The road is bounded to the north and south by tangled vegetation which looks impassable. You can continue East into the forest or West to Hengemire.

> w
You move west.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs along the south side of the village green. The road continues East out of the village, entering a forest about half a kilometre away. By the side of the road, almost hidden by the grass, is a milestone. To the South stands the village church, while some distance due North you see a well. You can also go North and NW onto the village green or West back along the road.  The market is now in full swing on the village green to the NW.

> n
You move north.

SE Corner of Village Green
You stand on the southeast corner of the village green. On the other side of the road, due south, lies the village church. The eastern side of the village green is hemmed in by impenetrable vegetation with forest beyond that, but you can go North, NW, West and SW from here. Here you see a stall, overflowing with vegetables, with the market gardener Freddy Awstin and his wife Iris, standing behind it, yelling out their spiel as they serve customers. The customers stand three or four deep around the stall, with more arriving by the minute.

> w
You move west.

South Side of Village Green
You are on the south side of the village green. This wide expanse of grass is bounded on the south side by the road that runs through the village, while to the north you see the village cross. You can go in all directions from here.  The market is in full swing, the village green is crowded with stalls and people, and here stands the blacksmith's stall with the blacksmith calling out the quality of his wares.

> say hello to blacksmith
You say hello to the blacksmith and he greets you.

"Good morrow to you, kind sir," he says to you. "Are you interested in buying some of my tools?"

> buy axe
You buy an axe suitable for chopping wood from the blacksmith for 2 gold coins, thanking him as you take the axe.

> se
You move southeast.

> n

In Farmyard
You are in the cobble-stoned yard of a small farm, which is enclosed on three sides by farm buildings. A farmhouse lies on the west side with a tall barn to the north, while the east side is made up of a row of stables and byres. Beyond the barn and the stables you see a field with various farm animals grazing in it. The road is to the South through a gap in the hedgerow.  Piled high here are some short logs.

> drop all except axe
Ok, you put down the lamplighter, the unlit oil lamp and the bent connecting rod.

> chop logs
You take your jacket off, spit on the palms of your hands and, gripping the shaft of the axe in both hands, you set to work chopping the logs into firewood. It takes you quite a while and by the time you have nearly finished you are perspiring heavily.

Unbeknownst to you, the farmer has been watching you from his farmhouse and as you are chopping the last of the logs he comes out with a sieve in his hand.

"Thanks for chopping that lot," he says to you, handing you the sieve. "That lot will last a week or more if I'm careful." He goes into a barn and wheels out a wheelbarrow. He piles the cut logs into the barrow and then wheels it into into his farmhouse, whistling as he goes.

Also here is a lamplighter, an unlit oil lamp and a bent connecting rod.

> get all

You are on a road that runs North-South through a sleepy little village towards the river further south. Here you see several cottages and larger houses that sit in neatly-tended gardens, the nearest one being accessible via a gate which is to the East. On the west side of the road is a large white-washed cottage with a sign above the door which reads "Village Store". The door leading in to the store is closed and a hand-written notice has been nailed to it which reads "Gone to Hengemire Market - Back later".

> e
You move east.

In Garden of Cottage
You are in the garden of the cottage on a path that winds through neat little flower beds to a yellow-painted door. By the door against the wall of the cottage there is a wooden bench.  Sitting on the bench here is a little old lady, she is wrapped up warmly in your fur coat.

Edwina looks up as you approach. "Hello again young man," she says to you hopefully. "Have you borrowed a sieve yet?"

> sieve dirt
You get down on your hands and knees and start to sieve the soil in Edwina's flower beds, closely supervised by Edwina who is worried you will damage her plants.

After about 20 minutes, during which time you reckon you have sieved the soil in most of the flower beds, you finally find Edwina's key. She squeals with delight as you hand it to her and as she unlocks the door to her cottage and goes in she tells you to wait there.

She comes out a minute or so later with her purse in her hand and she hands you a silver coin. "Thank you so much for finding my key, young Alaric," she says to you. "You really are a nice helpful young man."

She takes the sieve from you. "I'll return the sieve to farmer Feighan for you," she tells you.

Edwina then takes your right hand in her hands and, turning it palm up, looks closely at it. "You are destined for great things, Alaric Blackmoon" she tells you somewhat enigmatically. "I have the gift of second sight and am seldom wrong."

She stands up on tiptoe and kisses your cheek, then goes into her cottage and shuts the door.....

In Garden of Cottage

> w

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

> in
You move in.

In Tavern
You are in the main room of "The Ferryman Awaits" tavern. In contrast to the inn at Hengemire, it is a dark, scruffy place that reeks of fish. The tavernkeeper is lounging in a chair in front of three large barrels of ale that rest on x-shaped trestles against the wall of the tavern opposite the door. Seated on benches around the one table the tavern boasts are a number of fishermen, who stare at you suspiciously.

> buy beer
You tell the tavernkeeper you want to buy a tankard of beer for the blacksmith.

"Very well, sir, " he says politely. "George's favourite is Triple-X so I'll give you some of that."

He takes a tankard down from where it was hanging from the rafters, fills it from the right hand barrel and hands it to you.

"That'll be one silver coin please," he says holding out a calloused hand. You give him the silver coin whereupon he bites it to make sure it is genuine before putting it inside the pocket of his apron.

> out
You move out.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

> n
You move north.

Road through Village

> n
You move north.

Junction in Road
You are at a junction in the East-West road, where another road goes South towards the river Sutlej, entering a small village that nestles on the bank of the river. A wide lane leads off NE through the trees and you can see a column of smoke rising from a chimney in the gaps between the branches in that direction. By the side of the road here there is a triple-armed signpost.

> ne
You move northeast.

Outside Forge
The lane has led you to a blacksmith's forge, a low brick-built building with a slate roof that occupies a clearing in the woodland.  A pair of large wooden doors are open either side of a wide doorway that leads In to the forge. There is a large freshly painted sign above the doors of the forge.

> in
You move in.

Inside Forge
You stand inside the forge building, a dark-shadowed place smelling strongly of smoke and hot metal. It is dominated by the forge itself, the fire of which glows red hot in the darkness. The fire is being kept hot by the air blown into it by a large bellows which is being worked by the blacksmith's apprentice. The doors lead Out to the lane.  Standing here by his anvil, working some white hot metal, is the blacksmith George Steers.

> say to blacksmith straighten rod
You show the tankard of beer to the blacksmith and you ask him if he will straighten the rod for you.

He takes the rod from you and bracing the bent part against his raised right knee, he pulls back steadily on the ends of the rod, his arm muscles bulging with the effort. He pauses and checks the straightness a couple of times by sight and eventually he hands you a perfectly straight connecting rod.

"I've bin lookin' forward to this since you came earlier," he says, taking the tankard from you and draining it in several mouthfuls. "Ahhh! There's nothing like a nice cool tankard of Triple-X from the 'Ferryman Awaits'!" he exclaims.

The blacksmith resumes working the metal on his anvil, muttering instructions to Willy as he does so.

> out
You move out.

> w
You move west.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.

> w
You move west.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road and to the north the mountains thrust above them into the sky. Gaps in the hedgerow lead North to a farmyard and South to a sawmill.

> s
You move south.

By Sawmill
You are outside a sawmill which stands on the bank of the fast-flowing river that runs down to the Sutlej river. The road is to the North.  There is silence from the sawmill and there doesn't seem to be any wood being sawn at the moment.

You call out to the sawyer, who comes out of the sawmill. When he sees the straightened rod in your hands he grins with delight.

"Thank you so very much," he tells you as you hand the rod to him. "Wait here, it won't take me long to fit this to the machinery and I can cut that wood you want."

He goes back into the sawmill and you wait. After about 5 minutes you hear the waterwheel start turning and then the loud buzzing of the saw as it cuts through wood. A bit more time passes and then the sawyer comes back out of the sawmill carrying several planks of wood in his arms.

"There you go," he says as you take the wood from him. "I've cut wood for Denny before so I know how wide he wants it, the planks are long enough for him to trim down to size. Now, if you'll excuse me I have lots of work to catch up on."

You thank the sawyer and he walks back into his sawmill. The sound of the saw buzzing away recommences seconds later.

> n
You move north.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road and to the north the mountains thrust above them into the sky. Gaps in the hedgerow lead North to a farmyard and South to a sawmill.

> e
You move east.

East-West Road

> s
You move south.

On River Bank
You are on the south bank of the river Sutlej, where a path runs East-West along the bank as far as the eye can see. Here a jetty juts out into the river which you can get on to by going South. Across the river you can see Direwood forest on the far shore with the black mass of cloud looming above it.  Pulled up onto the bank of the river here is a ferryboat.

> s
You move south.

On Jetty
You are on the jetty which projects out from the bank into the river Sutlej. If there was a boat moored here you could walk Down the steps into it, but as there isn't the only way you can go is North onto the river bank. Sitting here, gazing wistfully out at the river, is the ferryman.

As you walk onto the landing stage with the planks of wood in your arms, Denny looks up and his eyes go wide with astonishment and he leaps to his feet.

"Blimey, you got me some wood!" he says taking the planks from your arms. "I can get to work fixing me boat." Then his face falls and he looks rather unhappy.

"Blast! I'm still gonna need a hammer and some nails before I can do that," he tells you. "D'ya fink you can find those for me?"

You promise the ferryman that you will try to find a hammer and some nails. He puts the wood down onto the landing stage sits down beside it.

> n
You move north.

On River Bank
You are on the south bank of the river Sutlej, where a path runs East-West along the bank as far as the eye can see. Here a jetty juts out into the river which you can get on to by going South. Across the river you can see Direwood forest on the far shore with the black mass of cloud looming above it.  Pulled up onto the bank of the river here is a ferryboat.

A strong gust of cold wind blows down from the mountains as you walk away from the landing stage. Further up the road you notice a woman walking towards you holding her coat around her to keep out the cold.

Suddenly a stronger flurry of air blows the woman's hat off of her head and into the air. You watch as the hat is wafted high into the air by the zephyr and it comes to rest high in the branches of the oak tree a bit further north.

> n
You move north.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.  Lily Peebles is here.

The woman rushes up to you as you approach her.

"Please, kind sir," she pleads with you. "My name is Lily Peebles and my hat has been blown into the tree by the wind. Would you climb the tree and fetch it down for me?"

She stands there eagerly awaiting your answer.

> say yes
(to Lily Peebles)

You tell Lily your name and assure her that you will get her hat down from the tree.

"Oh thank you so much, master Blackmoon," she says, and steps back to allow you room to climb the tree.

> drop all
Ok, you put down the lamplighter, the unlit oil lamp and the axe.

> climb up tree
You tell Lily that it won't take you a minute and you climb up the oak tree and into the branches as high as you can go.

In Branches of Tree
You are perched amongst the branches of the oak tree, as high as you can safely go. The only way you can go is to climb down the tree to the ground.  Above you in the branches, just within reach, is a woman's hat. Lily stands on the ground below the tree, looking anxiously up at you.

> get hat
You reach up as far as you can stretch and manage to hook a finger over the crown of the hat. It takes you a couple of attempts but you manage to dislodge the hat from the twigs it is snagged on and you catch it as it falls.

> wear hat
Ok, you put on the lady's hat.

> d
You climb down from the tree to the ground, being careful not to slip.....

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.  Also here is a lamplighter, an unlit oil lamp and an axe.  Lily Peebles is here.

As you reach the ground Lily reaches out and takes her hat off your head.

"The colour doesn't suit you dear," she says with a chuckle as she checks the hat for damage before putting it on her own head. "Thank you so much for getting it down for me," she tells you. "I wish I had something to stop the wind blowing it off!"

You reply that it was no trouble at all and go to walk away, but Lily touches your arm to stop you.

"I was going to Hengemire market but this incident has quite exhausted me," she tells you. "You wouldn't be a dear and pop along there and get me some fresh vegetables from Freddie Awstin, would you? I'll make it worth your while!"

You tell Lily that you will indeed get her some vegetables from the market at Hengemire.

"Oh thank you, Alaric," she says gratefully, and she opens her purse and takes out a gold coin, which she hands to you.

"That'll buy you a basket of vegetables from Freddie Awstin's stall," she tells you. "Now, I'm not waiting out here in the cold for you so you'll find me in the "Ferryman's."

She then walks into the tavern, leaving you standing alone in the road wondering how many more favors you have got to do for people!

Bridge over River
You are on a bridge which crosses a narrow river that flows down from the mountains to join the Sutlej river further south. The forest is thinner here and you can see the edge of the forest further East where the road emerges into daylight. The road also goes SW deeper into the forest.

> sw
You move southwest.

Road through Forest
You are on the road from Hengemire in the depths of a dark forest. The canopy above you, although largely bare of leaves, is so thick it blots out most of the sunlight. The road goes West to Hengemire and bends to the NE as it goes deeper into the forest.

> w
You move west.

Road through Old Forest
You are just inside the forest on the road from Hengemire to Chaldon. To the West the road emerges from the trees while going East will take you deeper into the forest.

> w
You move west.

Road East of Hengemire
You are about 100 metres from where the road from Hengemire enters the Old Forest. The road is bounded to the north and south by tangled vegetation which looks impassable. You can continue East into the forest or West to Hengemire.

> w
You move west.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs along the south side of the village green. The road continues East out of the village, entering a forest about half a kilometre away. By the side of the road, almost hidden by the grass, is a milestone. To the South stands the village church, while some distance due North you see a well. You can also go North and NW onto the village green or West back along the road.  The market is now in full swing on the village green to the NW.

> n
You move north.

SE Corner of Village Green
You stand on the southeast corner of the village green. On the other side of the road, due south, lies the village church. The eastern side of the village green is hemmed in by impenetrable vegetation with forest beyond that, but you can go North, NW, West and SW from here. Here you see a stall, overflowing with vegetables, with the market gardener Freddy Awstin and his wife Iris, standing behind it, yelling out their spiel as they serve customers. The customers stand three or four deep around the stall, with more arriving by the minute.

You notice a young woman pick up a ewer from behind the stall here and walk north towards the well in the NE corner of the village green. You guess she going to fetch some fresh water for Freddy and Iris - maybe she is their daughter?

> n
You move north.

East Side of Village Green
You are on the east side of the village green. You can go North, South, West, NW and SW but to the East lies thick vegetation with the forest beyond that.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A draper's stall stands here, stacked high with gaily coloured bolts of cloth and the draper himself is here, shouting out his spiel.

> n
You move north.

NE Side of Village Green
You are on the northeast side of the village green, by the well. Beyond, to the North and NE you see some of the cottages and other dwellings belonging to the residents of Hengemire. To the east lies thick impassable vegetation with the forest beyond that.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people.

The woman you saw by the stall earlier is here talking to another, older, woman. They finish their conversation as you approach, the older woman walks away and the younger woman puts her ewer down beside the well. She lowers the bucket down the well so that it fills with water then starts to turn the handle to raise it. As the mechanism is old and the bucket is heavy, she is struggling to turn the handle.

NE Side of Village Green
You are on the northeast side of the village green, by the well. Beyond, to the North and NE you see some of the cottages and other dwellings belonging to the residents of Hengemire. To the east lies thick impassable vegetation with the forest beyond that.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people.  Also here is a ewer.  A woman is here struggling to turn the handle of the windlass.

> say hello
Which trader in particular do you want to talk to?

> help jacqui
You offer to help the woman raise the bucket, telling her your name. "Thank you so much master Alaric," she says gratefully. "My name is Jacqui Awstin."

You grab the handle of the windlass and she steps back to allow you room as you quickly turn the handle to raise the bucket up the well shaft.

She fills her ewer from the bucket and thanks you profusely.

"Wait here a minute," she tells you and you watch as she walks away to the south, becoming lost to view behind the multitude of people. She returns a minute or two later bearing a basket of vegetables which she hands to you.

"These are fresh vegetables from my parents' stall," she tells you. "A small token of my appreciation."

Planting a kiss on your cheek, she walks off into the crowd and is lost to view.

NE Side of Village Green

To the east lies thick impassable vegetation with the forest beyond that.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people.

> s
You move south.

East Side of Village Green
You are on the east side of the village green. You can go North, South, West, NW and SW but to the East lies thick vegetation with the forest beyond that.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A draper's stall stands here, stacked high with gaily coloured bolts of cloth and the draper himself is here, shouting out his spiel.

You hear a flutter of wings and look up to see a magpie fly over your head, carrying something in its beak - you are sure it is the same one you saw in the graveyard.

Its flight takes it towards the cesspool and as it gets near someone throws something at it. As it swerves in the air to avoid the missile, it drops whatever it was carrying in its beak. The object falls into the weeds surrounding the cesspool, the magpie itself flies off into the trees to the west of Hengemire and is lost to view.

> s
You move south.

SE Corner of Village Green

The customers stand three or four deep around the stall, with more arriving by the minute.

> sw
You move southwest.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs through Hengemire along the southern edge of the village green. Directly North, in the centre of the green, you see a stone cross. The road continues East and West, the village cesspool is SW, the church SE, and to the South are the village stocks and pillory. The market is now in full swing on the village green to the north.

> sw
You move southwest.

By Cesspool
You are in the southwest corner of the village green, by a stand of weeds which partly conceals the cesspool. You can go North, East and NE from here.

As you walk near the cesspool a weak shaft of sunlight pokes through the cloud cover and illuminates the weeds growing in front of the pool. In amongst the weeds you see something shiny glinting in the sunlight for a few seconds before the light fades and the glinting stops. You mark the spot in your mind's eye.

> drop all
Ok, you put down the lamplighter, the unlit oil lamp, the axe and the basket of vegetables.

> search weeds
You bend down and search for the shiny object that you saw glinting in the weeds.

At first you cannot find it, then you spot the object - it is a hat pin - near the far edge of the weeds. You stretch out to reach for it and as your fingers close around the pin you hear a loud bleat behind you and the sound of small hooves running along the ground. You glance behind you and see the billygoat running full pelt towards you, its head lowered in butting position.....

Press Any Key....
KER-POW! The billygoat's horns hit you right up the "Khyber" and you are catapulted through the air over the clump of weeds.....

Press Any Key....
SPLASH! You land face first into the cesspool, which is filled with the most noisome muck you have ever encountered. You scramble to your feet covered in absolute filth and you stand there up to your knees in the black water, wiping the mess and lumps of unmentionable things off of you with your hands.....

Press Any Key....
You then become aware of laughter and look up to see a group of people from the market who had witnessed the incident and are pointing at you and roaring their heads off. You manage to get the worst lumps of mess off of your clothes before you clamber painfully out of the pool. The people become aware of the smell that now emanates from you and they back away, holding hands and handkerchiefs over their noses, as you stand there with black water dripping off you.

You look around for the billygoat, hoping to exact some revenge on it for your sore bottom, but it is nowhere to be seen!

By Cesspool
You are in the southwest corner of the village green, by a stand of weeds which partly conceals the cesspool. You can go North, East and NE from here.  Also here is a lamplighter, an unlit oil lamp, an axe and a basket of vegetables.

> get all
Ok, you pick up the lamplighter, the unlit oil lamp, the axe and the basket of vegetables.

> ne
You move northeast.

Road through Village

> ne

SE Corner of Village Green
You stand on the southeast corner of the village green. On the other side of the road, due south, lies the village church. The eastern side of the village green is hemmed in by impenetrable vegetation with forest beyond that, but you can go North, NW, West and SW from here. Here you see a stall, overflowing with vegetables, with the market gardener Freddy Awstin and his wife Iris, standing behind it, yelling out their spiel as they serve customers. The customers stand three or four deep around the stall, with more arriving by the minute.

People hold their noses as you approach them and move away from you in disgust at the smell of the cesspool on you.

"Oii! Clear orf, ya smelly git!" Freddie Awstin shouts at you. "You'll make all me veg smell with that stink!"

> n
You move north.

East Side of Village Green
You are on the east side of the village green. You can go North, South, West, NW and SW but to the East lies thick vegetation with the forest beyond that.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A draper's stall stands here, stacked high with gaily coloured bolts of cloth and the draper himself is here, shouting out his spiel.

The draper nearly faints from the awful smell you are giving off and a couple of customers hurry away from his stall as you draw near.

"Be off!" he squeaks at you. "You need a few buckets of water thrown over you!"

> n
You move north.

NE Side of Village Green
You are on the northeast side of the village green, by the well. Beyond, to the North and NE you see some of the cottages and other dwellings belonging to the residents of Hengemire. To the east lies thick impassable vegetation with the forest beyond that.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people.

> pour water over head
You pick up the bucket of water and pour it over your head to wash the mess off your clothes. You have to repeat the process a few times before all the mess has disappeared. You are now clean, but your clothes are very wet.

> sw
You move southwest.

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A stall selling all sorts of armour stands here, the armourer is sitting by the side of the stall working on an armoured gauntlet.

> w
You move west.

By Inn
You are standing on the west side of the village green, by the large building, which a sign hanging from the wall by the door declares itself to be the "Dragonslayer's Arms" inn. The inn door leads In, going North takes you to the entrance to the inn yard and you can go South back along the track to the road. The village green itself lies to the East, SE and NE.  The market is now in full swing over on the village green and the noise of the traders yelling out their spiel is deafening.

> in
You move in.

East End of Inn
You are in the main room of the Dragonslayer's Arms inn. It is a large, dark room with a low, beamed ceiling and a stone floor strewn with rushes. Tallow candles gutter on several tables and on various places around the inn. The room smells of wine and ale, but it seems to be well-kept. Against the north wall are a row of barrels on trestles, in front of which is a plank of wood, supported by two tables, which is known as the "bar". The room extends West and the door leads Out.  The inn is busy with people who have been to, or are going to, the market and traders taking a welcome break from yelling out their wares at their stalls.  Sarah Ann Roffey is here.

> w
You move west.

West End of Inn
You are at the west end of the main room of the inn. This end of the room is dominated by a stone pit in which burns a blazing fire, the smoke from which rises errantly towards a chimney set above it on four square pillars. The south wall is covered by a large tapestry. Opposite that a door leads North and the other end of the room is East.

> dry clothes
You sit as close to the fire as you can without burning yourself and wait while your clothes dry. A column of steam rises from you as the heat evaporates the water soaked into your clothes and you change position a few times to allow the warmth to get to all parts of your body.

Eventually your clothes are dried and you can continue with what you were doing.

> e
You move east.

East End of Inn
You are in the main room of the Dragonslayer's Arms inn. It is a large, dark room with a low, beamed ceiling and a stone floor strewn with rushes. Tallow candles gutter on several tables and on various places around the inn. The room smells of wine and ale, but it seems to be well-kept. Against the north wall are a row of barrels on trestles, in front of which is a plank of wood, supported by two tables, which is known as the "bar". The room extends West and the door leads Out.  The inn is busy with people who have been to, or are going to, the market and traders taking a welcome break from yelling out their wares at their stalls.  Sarah Ann Roffey is here.

As you reach this end of the inn you hear raised voices and look over to where they are coming from. A couple of elderly men seem to be in the middle of an argument about a game of dominos.....

"...but Eric, you can't have a proper game when you're missing a double-six," one old man is saying. "Of course, you can Ernie," his opponent responds. "Quit yer moanin' and get on with the game. If you hadn't've lost it in the first place, you wouldn't be complaining!"

The men continue their game but Eric continues to mutter to himself as they play.

East End of Inn
You are in the main room of the Dragonslayer's Arms inn. It is a large, dark room with a low, beamed ceiling and a stone floor strewn with rushes. Tallow candles gutter on several tables and on various places around the inn. The room smells of wine and ale, but it seems to be well-kept. Against the north wall are a row of barrels on trestles, in front of which is a plank of wood, supported by two tables, which is known as the "bar". The room extends West and the door leads Out.  The inn is busy with people who have been to, or are going to, the market and traders taking a welcome break from yelling out their wares at their stalls.  Two elderly men playing dominos sit at a table here, while Sarah Ann the barmaid serves a never-ending stream of customers wanting refreshment.

> ask eric about domino
You ask Eric about the domino that they have lost.

"That doddering old twit sitting there lost it," he tells you, glaring at Ernie across the table. "Dropped the box of dominos as we were sitting down."

He pauses to place a domino on the table with a look of triumph on his face. Ernie looks closely at the domino that Eric has just placed and studies the dominos in his hand with a frown.

"We got down on our hands and knees and found all of 'em," Eric continues. "But we couldn't find the double six, even Sarah looked and she couldn't see with her young eyes."

> ask ernie about domino
You ask Ernie about the domino that they have lost.

"I was carrying the box of dominos as we were walking over to sit at this table," Ernie tells you. "When that decrepit old fool bumped into me, knocking the box out of me 'and and the dominos went all over the floor."

He pauses as Eric places a domino on the table with a look of triumph on his face. Ernie looks closely at the domino that Eric has just placed and studies the dominos in his hand with a frown.

"We got down on our hands and knees and found all of 'em," Ernie continues. "But we couldn't find the double six, even Sarah looked and she couldn't see with her young eyes."

> ask sarah about men
You ask Sarah Ann about the two men playing dominos. She stops to talk to you and have a breather at the same time.

"Those two are Eric & Ernie. They have known each other since they were children. They're in here most nights," she tells you. "If it's not dominos, they'll be playing cards, if it ain't cards it'll be shove 'appenny. Whatever they're playing, they'll always find something to moan about."

> search floor
You get down on your hands and knees and search around in the rushes on the floor under the tables and you find a domino which you pick up.

> give domino to ernie
You hand the domino to Ernie, who is absolutely delighted as he takes it from you.

"Thank you, young man. We can play our game properly now!" he tells you. He then reaches up and takes something from around his neck and hands it to you.

"I found this deep underground long ago when I was a miner," he tells you. "I ain't gotta clue what it is or what the runes mean but it's brought me luck all these years. I'd like you to have it as a thank you for finding our domino."

You decide not to argue with Ernie and you accept the gift with thanks, slipping the thong over your head and tucking the talisman inside your shirt so it lies against your skin.

Ernie looks at Eric, saying, "Oii you, show the man some appreciation!" Eric glowers at Ernie but he reaches into his pocket and gives you a gold coin.

"There ya go mate, get yerself a drink with that," he tells you, turning back to his game of dominos.

> x talisman
A talisman made from a lump of a hard grey substance, crudely carved in the shape of a goblin-like creature, and hung on a leather thong. There are some runes inscribed on the talisman.  You have as much of an idea of what this object is as Ernie does... you wonder to yourself if Magor might know what it is?

> out
You move out.

By Inn
You are standing on the west side of the village green, by the large building, which a sign hanging from the wall by the door declares itself to be the "Dragonslayer's Arms" inn. The inn door leads In, going North takes you to the entrance to the inn yard and you can go South back along the track to the road. The village green itself lies to the East, SE and NE.  The market is now in full swing over on the village green and the noise of the traders yelling out their spiel is deafening.

North Side of Village Green
You are on the north side of the village green, where a wide track leads North towards the mountains,leading between the cottages which stand in clusters to the NW, NE and East. You can also go West, South, SE and SW across the green from here.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. There is a lampmaker's stall here.

> n
You move north.

Mountain Track
You're on a track that zigzags up and down the rough scree-covered slope of the mountain. A trail leads off northwest towards a canyon, and the track continues to wind Up the mountain, entering the snow several hundred metres above. You have an excellent view of Hengemire village to the South.

> nw
You move northwest.

Entrance to Canyon
You're near the entrance to a narrow canyon in the mountains. You see that the canyon leads to a rocky outcrop at the western end on which stands a tall, slender tower. You can go West to the tower or SE back to the junction in the track.

> w
You move west.

By Tower
The canyon opens out to the top of a rocky outcrop overlooking the surrounding countryside. Perched about 3 metres from the edge of the outcrop is the tall tower, which soars above you for at least 50 metres. A small bell hangs from a metal bracket beside a large circular slab of rock which covers the entrance to the tower.

> ring bell
Ding-a-ling!

> ring bell
Ding-a-ling!

> ring bell
Ding-a-ling!

On the third ring you hear Magor call out:

"Come on up, I'll open the door!"

The rock slab rolls ponderously to one side.

By Tower
The canyon opens out to the top of a rocky outcrop overlooking the surrounding countryside. Perched about 3 metres from the edge of the outcrop is the tall tower, which soars above you for at least 50 metres. The slab has rolled to one side to reveal a round opening leading West into the foot of the tower. A small bell hangs from a metal bracket beside the entrance.

> w
You move west.

Foot of Stairway
You're at the foot of some worn steps that spiral up through the solid rock. The round opening to the tower is open and leads east.

> u
You move up.

Magor's Chamber
You're in the main chamber of Magor's tower, a smoky, dark-cornered room that is full of mostly incomprehensible things. There are hundreds of books and scrolls in piles and on shelves, and on a long table by one wall, a strange thaumaturgical apparatus bubbles and seethes away.  Magor is standing by his workbench, closely watching the apparatus which is hissing and bubbling away merrily.  There is another chair similar to Magor's on the opposite side of the fireplace. While there are other doors and staircases leading off this chamber, the only exit you can take is Down.

Magor turns from his work and frowns when he sees you and he reluctantly bids you sit down, which you do. "So, I see you are back, young Alaric, how can I help you this time?"

> ask magor about talisman
You show the talisman to Magor and ask him what it is.

He takes it from you and studies it closely for a minute or two. He goes to his table and, selecting a thick tome from a shelf, starts turning the pages. He finds what he was looking for and nods to himself.

"I thought so. It is an ancient charm against Tunnel Wights," he tells you. "The runes spell out the word 'Dispellarius'. If you are underground and are confronted by a Tunnel Wight, you have to say that word and it will be banished." You say the word "Dispellarius" to yourself several times so you will remember what the runes mean.

Handing the talisman back to you, as you put it over your head he warns you, "You must be wearing or at least carrying the talisman in your hand, for the charm to work. Of course, there's only one problem with Tunnel Wights - finding out their name is next to impossible!"

> ask magor about tunnel wights
You ask Magor about Tunnel Wights.

"Tunnel Wights are similar to Barrow Wights," the sorcerer tells you. "They are the lost souls of miners who have perished in the deep tunnels of mines. If you ever see one you must either banish it using the talisman or run for your life - if it touches any part of your body it will devour your soul instantly!"

> ask magor about barrow wights
You ask Magor about Barrow Wights.

"Barrow Wights are the spirits of those buried in barrow tombs," Magor tells you. "They were usually great Kings, Queens or Chieftains and are harmless unless the bones of the buried person are disturbed."

> ask magor about father
You ask Magor about his father.

"My father was a very powerful sorcerer," Magor tells you proudly. "He was a young man when he helped to design Kolt's tomb. It was built in a secret location so that looters would not be able to find it."

> ask magor about kolt
You ask Magor what sort of a King Kolt was. He smiles and looks wistful.

"I remember my father telling me epic tales of King Kolt when I was a child," he tells you. He was a fearless warrior who led his armies into battle himself and always put the safety of his men before that of himself. He brought a lasting peace to Hecate after he defeated the Xixon, but now they have returned - what is going to become of Hecate now?!"

> d
You take your leave of Magor, thanking him for his help.

"No trouble at all, old chap," he tells you. "Good luck with your quest!"

You walk down the stairway, nearly falling down as you forget about the wonky step again, and leave the tower.

The market is in full swing, the village green is crowded with stalls and people, and here stands the blacksmith's stall with the blacksmith calling out the quality of his wares.

Road through Village

You can also go North and NW onto the village green or West back along the road.  The market is now in full swing on the village green to the NW.

> e
You move east.

Road East of Hengemire
You are about 100 metres from where the road from Hengemire enters the Old Forest. The road is bounded to the north and south by tangled vegetation which looks impassable. You can continue East into the forest or West to Hengemire.

> e
You move east.

Road through Old Forest
You are just inside the forest on the road from Hengemire to Chaldon. To the West the road emerges from the trees while going East will take you deeper into the forest.

> e
You move east.

Road through Forest
You are on the road from Hengemire in the depths of a dark forest. The canopy above you, although largely bare of leaves, is so thick it blots out most of the sunlight. The road goes West to Hengemire and bends to the NE as it goes deeper into the forest.

> ne
You move northeast.

Bridge over River
You are on a bridge which crosses a narrow river that flows down from the mountains to join the Sutlej river further south. The forest is thinner here and you can see the edge of the forest further East where the road emerges into daylight. The road also goes SW deeper into the forest.

> e
You move east.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road and to the north the mountains thrust above them into the sky. Gaps in the hedgerow lead North to a farmyard and South to a sawmill.

> e
You move east.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.

> e
You move east.

Junction in Road
You are at a junction in the East-West road, where another road goes South towards the river Sutlej, entering a small village that nestles on the bank of the river. A wide lane leads off NE through the trees and you can see a column of smoke rising from a chimney in the gaps between the branches in that direction. By the side of the road here there is a triple-armed signpost.

> s
You move south.

Road through Village
You are on a road that runs North-South through a sleepy little village towards the river further south. Here you see several cottages and larger houses that sit in neatly-tended gardens, the nearest one being accessible via a gate which is to the East. On the west side of the road is a large white-washed cottage with a sign above the door which reads "Village Store". The door leading in to the store is closed and a hand-written notice has been nailed to it which reads "Gone to Hengemire Market - Back later".

> s
You move south.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

> in
You move in.

In Tavern
You are in the main room of "The Ferryman Awaits" tavern. In contrast to the inn at Hengemire, it is a dark, scruffy place that reeks of fish. The tavernkeeper is lounging in a chair in front of three large barrels of ale that rest on x-shaped trestles against the wall of the tavern opposite the door. Seated on benches around the one table the tavern boasts are a number of fishermen, who stare at you suspiciously.  The tavernkeeper, some drinkers and Lily Peebles are here.

Lily breaks off from chatting to the men in the tavern and looks at you in expectation as you walk into the tavern. Her face lights up when she sees that you have her basket of vegetables.

"Oh thank you so very much, master Alaric," she tells you, her voice slightly slurred from drink. "Here, go buy yerself a drink!"

She fumbles in her purse, takes out a gold coin and hands it to you.

"You did me a big favour going to the market for me," she tells you somewhat drunkenly. "I was able to have a lovely time chatting to the boys here!"

Lily turns back and resumes her chatting and laughing with the men in the tavern. You put the coin into your pouch and think about what you need to buy.

> give hat pin to lily
You give the hat pin to Lily and her face breaks into a huge smile as she sees what it is.

"That's just what I need to keep me 'at on me 'ead!" she tells you. She jabs the pin into the side of the hat on her head so hard it makes you wince! "There! That won't fly off in a hurry!" she says with a smile.

She reaches into a pocket of her coat and fetches out a gold coin which she flips into the air for you to catch.

"There ya go, fair exchange is no robbery," she tells you happily as you put the coin into your pouch.

> out
You move out.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

Junction in Road
You are at a junction in the East-West road, where another road goes South towards the river Sutlej, entering a small village that nestles on the bank of the river. A wide lane leads off NE through the trees and you can see a column of smoke rising from a chimney in the gaps between the branches in that direction. By the side of the road here there is a triple-armed signpost.

You hear someone whistling and you look in that direction to see the blacksmith George Steers walking down the lane from his forge towards you. As he reaches the junction he nods in greeting to you.

"Hello Master Blackmoon," he says cheerfully. "I've had enough for one day, I'm off home!"

You wish him well and he starts to walk south towards the village.

"I left young Willy in charge," he calls back to you. "He's well able to look after the place."

He walks south for a short distance then turns out of sight.

> ne
You move northeast.

Outside Forge
The lane has led you to a blacksmith's forge, a low brick-built building with a slate roof that occupies a clearing in the woodland.  A pair of large wooden doors are open either side of a wide doorway that leads In to the forge. There is a large freshly painted sign above the doors of the forge.

> in
You move in.

Inside Forge
You stand inside the forge building, a dark-shadowed place smelling strongly of smoke and hot metal. It is dominated by the forge itself, the fire of which glows red hot in the darkness. Willy the blacksmith's apprentice is here on his own. The doors lead Out to the lane.

> give axe to willy
You give the axe to Willy, asking him if he would like it as you have no further use for it.

"Wow," he tells you enthusiastically. "That is very kind of you, Master Blackmoon. I haven't got an axe in my collection yet."

He looks at the axe lovingly and tests the sharpness of the blade with his thumb, whereupon the razor sharp edge slices into his skin and it starts to bleed.

"Ouch! That hurt!" he cries and he pulls a grubby handkerchief out of his pocket and wraps it around his thumb to stem the bleeding.

"You ought to get that seen to," you tell him, "otherwise it might go bad and you'll have to have your thumb chopped off - or your hand!"

The boy looks at you in horror and runs out of the forge. "I'll get me mum to fix it," he tells you over his shoulder. "She's good wiv 'erbs an' stuff!".

"Hold your hand above your head," you call to him. "That'll help stop the bleeding."

The last you see of the boy he is running down the lane, clutching his axe with one hand and holding the other above his head.

Inside Forge
You stand inside the forge building, a dark-shadowed place smelling strongly of smoke and hot metal. It is dominated by the forge itself, the fire of which glows red hot in the darkness.

You notice something glinting on the floor of the forge after Willy has left - it is a gold coin. Willy must have pulled it out of his pocket when he took out the handkerchief. You bend down, pick the coin up off the floor and put it into your pouch, considering it payment for the axe you gave to Willy.

> search forge
You search the forge, but find nothing of any use.

> out
You move out.

> buy hammer
You buy a small hammer from the blacksmith for 1 gold coin.

> buy nails
You tell the blacksmith you would like to buy some nails.

"That'll be one gold coin for a kilo, sir," he tells you. Taking a gold coin from your pouch, you hand it to him. He then weighs out a kilo of iron nails and puts them into a paper bag, which he hands to you.

> n
You move north.

Middle of Village Green
You are roughly at the centre of the village green, standing by the stone cross. You have a good view of the whole village from this spot, which is slightly elevated above the rest of the green. You can go in all directions.  The market is in full swing and the village green is crowded with stalls and people. A stall selling all sorts of armour stands here, the armourer is sitting by the side of the stall working on an armoured gauntlet.

A man approaches the stall and the armourer greets him. The customer looks like a swordsman and you listen as the man places an order for some armour with the armourer. They haggle a bit over the price but eventually a deal is struck and sealed with a handshake. The man hands over a bag of money and walks away looking pleased with himself, while the armourer goes back to working on the gauntlet.

> buy chainmail
You tell the armourer you need the chainmail for protection but you have only have 3 gold coins to your name.

"Oh go on then," he says handing the hauberk to you. "Just don't tell everyone I was so charitable!"

You hand over the 3 gold coins and the armourer goes back to repairing the gauntlet.

> tell armourer about xixon
You tell the armourer that you intend to find the lost Axe of Kolt and try to return it to King Kolt so that he can fight the Xixon again. The armourer's mouth has dropped open in astonishment as you tell him.

"You must be stark raving bonkers," he tells you. "I wouldn't attempt that without a whole army at my back!"

You reply that one man might succeed where an army would fail, but the armourer is unconvinced.

> s
You move south.

South Side of Village Green
You are on the south side of the village green. This wide expanse of grass is bounded on the south side by the road that runs through the village, while to the north you see the village cross. You can go in all directions from here.  The market is in full swing, the village green is crowded with stalls and people, and here stands the blacksmith's stall with the blacksmith calling out the quality of his wares.

> se
You move southeast.

Road through Village
You are on the road that runs along the south side of the village green. The road continues East out of the village, entering a forest about half a kilometre away. By the side of the road, almost hidden by the grass, is a milestone. To the South stands the village church, while some distance due North you see a well. You can also go North and NW onto the village green or West back along the road.  The market is now in full swing on the village green to the NW.

> e
You move east.

Road East of Hengemire
You are about 100 metres from where the road from Hengemire enters the Old Forest. The road is bounded to the north and south by tangled vegetation which looks impassable. You can continue East into the forest or West to Hengemire.

Road through Forest
You are on the road from Hengemire in the depths of a dark forest. The canopy above you, although largely bare of leaves, is so thick it blots out most of the sunlight. The road goes West to Hengemire and bends to the NE as it goes deeper into the forest.

> ne
You move northeast.

Bridge over River
You are on a bridge which crosses a narrow river that flows down from the mountains to join the Sutlej river further south. The forest is thinner here and you can see the edge of the forest further East where the road emerges into daylight. The road also goes SW deeper into the forest.

You move east.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road and to the north the mountains thrust above them into the sky. Gaps in the hedgerow lead North to a farmyard and South to a sawmill.

> e
You move east.

East-West Road
You are on an East-West road that runs through open countryside. Tall hedgerows line the road on both sides and you cannot see over them, but a gap in the hedgerow on the north side of the road leads North to the track you came down from the mountains.

Junction in Road
You are at a junction in the East-West road, where another road goes South towards the river Sutlej, entering a small village that nestles on the bank of the river. A wide lane leads off NE through the trees and you can see a column of smoke rising from a chimney in the gaps between the branches in that direction. By the side of the road here there is a triple-armed signpost.

Road through Village
You are on a road that runs North-South through a sleepy little village towards the river further south. Here you see several cottages and larger houses that sit in neatly-tended gardens, the nearest one being accessible via a gate which is to the East. On the west side of the road is a large white-washed cottage with a sign above the door which reads "Village Store". The door leading in to the store is closed and a hand-written notice has been nailed to it which reads "Gone to Hengemire Market - Back later".

You move south.

Road through Village
You are outside a tavern called "The Ferryman Awaits" which lies on the west side of the road through the village. The road continues south to a landing stage on the bank of the river and you can go North back through the village towards the main road. Opposite the tavern on the east side of the road a majestic oak tree stands, its branches almost bare of its leaves, some of which have been swept into a pile at the side of the road.

> s
You move south.

On River Bank
You are on the south bank of the river Sutlej, where a path runs East-West along the bank as far as the eye can see. Here a jetty juts out into the river which you can get on to by going South. Across the river you can see Direwood forest on the far shore with the black mass of cloud looming above it.  Pulled up onto the bank of the river here is a ferryboat.

> s
You move south.

On Jetty
You are on the jetty which projects out from the bank into the river Sutlej. If there was a boat moored here you could walk Down the steps into it, but as there isn't the only way you can go is North onto the river bank. Sitting here, gazing wistfully out at the river, is the ferryman.  Also here are some planks of wood.

As you walk onto the landing stage with the hammer and bag of nails in your hand, Denny gets to his feet.

"Oh great, you got me a hammer and some nails," he says taking them from your hand and picking up the pile of planks. "Now I can mend me boat!"

He walks off to start work on repairing his ferry boat and you sit down on the landing stage while you wait. After only a few minutes you hear him sawing and hammering away, whistling and singing while he works.

After about an hour or so you hear him shout out for some help in refloating the boat, so you go down to the river bank and help him push the repaired ferry onto the river and watch as he rigs the sail and moors it alongside the landing stage. You then walk back onto the landing stage.

On Jetty
You are on the jetty which projects out from the bank into the river Sutlej. Below the jetty, moored by the flight of wooden steps, is a ferry boat with the ferryman Denny Joyce standing in it ready to cast off once you have boarded the ferry. You can go Down the wooden steps into the boat or North onto the riverbank.

> board boat

THE AXE OF KOLT - Chapter Two:

The Forest of Evil

As you walk up the shore of the river Sutlej towards Direwood Forest, you are struck by the silence. Apart from the sound of the river flowing behind you - which itself is oddly muted - there is no bird song and despite the wind that is blowing the trees are strangely silent.

The nearer you get to the edge of the forest, the stronger the sense of pure malevolence emanating from the interior becomes. You realise, however, that you must find your way through the forest to Galhexia's lair, confronting all evils and perils on the way, if you are to fulfil your quest.....

Press B then Enter to Begin Chapter 2 . . . . .

> b

On Shore of River by Jetty
You are on the gently sloping shore of the river Sutlej about 100 metres from the edge of a dense, dark forest, standing by the remains of a ruined jetty. The shoreline extends to the East and West and the forest is to the South along a beaten path that led from the end of the jetty.  In the sky above the forest, an ominous mass of black clouds seethe and writhe as if they were a manifestation of the evil that lies within.

> e
You move east.

On Shore of River e
You are standing on the shore of the river Sutlej, about 150 metres east of the ruined jetty. The shore here is very narrow as thick vegetation extends from the edge of the forest almost to the edge of the water. The shoreline continues to the East or you can go back West to where you waded ashore.  In the sky above the forest, an ominous mass of black clouds seethe and writhe as if they were a manifestation of the evil that lies within.

> x vegetation
Dense, tangled vegetation that reaches almost down to the water's edge. It is completely normal, lying as it does outside the forest and untainted by the evil that lies within.  Just here you notice that the vegetation is a bit higher, as if it is growing over something hidden by it.

> search vegetation
You search the vegetation, pulling apart the tangled stems and branches of the plants and bushes that have grown in profusion here, scratching your hands despite the thick callouses. About a metre in you find the front of a large object that has been overgrown by the foliage. Further investigation reveals that it is the prow of a small boat.

Clearing away more of the vegetation that has covered the boat, you drag it out onto the shore of the river.

On Shore of River by Jetty
You are on the gently sloping shore of the river Sutlej about 100 metres from the edge of a dense, dark forest, standing by the remains of a ruined jetty. Edge of Forest
You are standing on a dividing line between the open air of the river shore to the North and the dark gloom of the forest to the South. The path from the shore continues south into the forest meandering its way round the trees until it is lost to view.

Looking around you see nothing that could be a threat, but a sense of impending danger warns you that it might be a good idea to wear the chainmail you bought in Hengemire.

> wear chainmail
Ok, you put on the chainmail hauberk.

> s
You walk south from the edge of the forest, along the path which is quite overgrown in places and a couple of times you almost fall over as your feet become ensnared in the tough stems of the plants that trail across your way.

The feeling of malevolence increases as you penetrate deeper into the forest, but there is an eerie silence around you broken only by the occasional sound of a bird or animal - and even those noises do not sound natural.

After walking for about a quarter of a kilometre you reach a fork in the path. That strange sixth sense you possess - which causes a tingling sensation in your spine when you are being watched - manifests itself and so you stop and glance around you.

Fork in Path
You are at a fork in the path through the forest, surrounded in all directions by trees. It is quite gloomy here, the canopy overhead blocking direct sunlight from reaching you. The path continues South, going ever deeper into the forest, but another slightly narrower path goes off to the SW past a stunted sapling growing by the edge of the undergrowth here. The only other way you can go is North back to the edge of the forest and the river Sutlej.

Some distance away to the south you see the figure of a tall man walking along the path with his back to you. You only see him for a second or two before he turns southwest and disappears from view.

> look around
You look around you at the forest, concentrating on any movement, but all is deathly still around you. You cannot, however, shake off the feeling that someone - or something - is watching you from the cover of a tree trunk or in the dense vegetation hereabouts.

> x sapling
A small sapling trying to grow at the edge of the path, it looks like some variety of coniferous tree.  There are two short branches from the stem of the sapling, one sticking out from the left side with the other further up on the right.

> break left branch
You break one of the branches off the sapling. Almost as soon as you do that you notice a thick clear resin start oozing out of the scar left on the side of the sapling. You look at the branch that you broke off of the sapling and you decide it is of no use to you whatsoever so you toss it into the undergrowth amongst the trees.

> break right branch
You grab hold of the remaining branch in order to break it off, but suddenly a strange sixth sense tells you that now might not be the most appropriate time to do this. You therefore decide to leave the branch growing on the sapling for now.

> sw
You move southwest.

Bend in Path
You are at a bend in the path where it goes NE and West, although you can see another path to the SE which you can get to by going around the tree that stands at the corner. To the south lies tangled vegetation which grows in profusion around the trees that populate this forest, but to the NW it is somewhat clearer and in a small glade about 7 metres in that direction you see a large clump of tall plants.

You hear the unmistakable sound of a bowstring being released from your right side and you instinctively duck away in the opposite direction. You feel a blow on your right shoulder as an arrow slams into it, but fortunately the dense rings of the chainmail prove too thick for the warhead to penetrate and the arrow glances off into the vegetation between the trees!

As you have no means to fight back, you do not wait to let the bowman get a second chance and you run down the path for a distance until you reach a junction.

A Junction of Forest Paths
The path from the East has ended in a junction with another path which runs North - South. Over to the west you can see the shapes of what appear to be small cottages, but you are unable to go directly towards them because of the tangled vegetation hereabouts. Further North, however, you see one of the cottages which lies closer to the path.

As you reach the junction, you thank the stars that you were wearing the chainmail, which undoubtedly saved your life. You realise however that you must not venture along that path again until you have got some means of fighting whatever it is lurking there.

> n
You move north.

A thick blanket of leaves covers the path right up to the door of the cottage.

The sap oozing from the scar on the sapling will set very soon!

PLOP! You feel something drop onto your shoulder and turn your head to see a large evil-looking spider crouched just inches away, stabbing at your shoulder with huge venomous fangs, but failing to penetrate your clothing. You feel its octet of eyes fasten on the bare flesh of your neck.....!

> brush spider
You brush the spider off of your shoulder with your hand and it falls to the floor, where it lands on its back on the carpet of leaves. It lays there scrabbling its legs, trying to turn itself right way up so it can escape into the undergrowth.

N-S Path in Forest

> stamp on spider

The spider's legs scrabble frantically and it tries futilely to pierce your boots with its vicious fangs. You press down a bit harder on its body and the legs go still as the spider finally dies with a crunch of chitin.
